Gerhart v. State


Case Number: F-2014-726


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2015 OK CR 12; 360 P.3d 1194; 2015 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 13; 43 Media L. Rep. 3078



October 7, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE RAY C. ELLIOTT, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's communication, an email sent to a senator telling him to have a bill heard in the legislative committee and ensure it was passed out of committee, was pure political advocacy, available to every citizen; [2]-Defendant's threat to "dig into" the past of the senator and his family and associates did not accuse of threaten to accuse the senator or anyone of a crime and thus, did not amount to blackmail under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 1488 (2011); [3]-Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 1488 (2011) was unconstitutionally applied to defendant, as his email fell within the protections of the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, charged dismissed.

 

202 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nelson


Case Number: S-2014-924


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2015 OK CR 10; 356 P.3d 1113; 2015 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 10



September 19, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE BILL HIDDLE, SPECIAL JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not abuse its discretion when it ruled that the initial stop was illegal, as the State failed to present sufficient facts at the motion hearing to demonstrate the stop was reasonable pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 11-604 (2011), or introduce a relevant municipal ordinance which would have enabled the State to argued in the alternative that the stop was reasonable under the ordinance; [2]-Defendant's alleged obstructive behavior was not the product of the officer's illegal stop, but was an independent and voluntary act which broke the link to any taint caused by the illegal stop and thus, the trial court erred when it suppressed all evidence related to defendant's obstruction and resisting arrest charges.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

Leftwich v. State


Case Number: F-2013-1156


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2015 OK CR 5; 350 P.3d 149; 2015 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 8



May 22, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE CINDY TRUONG, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Leftwich v. Court of Crim. Appeals of Okla., 2011 OK 80, 262 P.3d 750, 2011 Okla. LEXIS 83 (Okla., 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A "candidate" for purposes of Okla. Stat. tit. 26, §§ 16-107 and 108 was properly described by the definition in Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 187, and the Ethics Code; [2]-The term "withdraw" in Okla. Stat. tit. 26, §§ 16-107 and 16-108 was not exclusively confined to filing a notice of withdrawal of candidacy; a candidate who had not yet filed a Declaration of Candidacy might, by her actions, withdraw from a race; [3]-Application of the definition of "candidate" in Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 187, to Okla. Stat. tit. 26, § 16-108, did not render the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Arganbright v. State

Lockett v. State


Case Number: D-2000-1330; D-2003-829


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2014 OK CR 3; 329 P.3d 755; 2014 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 3



April 18, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Cross Reference with Oklahoma Supreme Court. Case No. 112741.
Lockett v. Evans, 2014 OK 28, 2014 Okla. LEXIS 35 (Okla., 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where the state supreme court transferred a joint application for a stay of execution to the instant court (the court of criminal appeals) to decide whether a stay should be issued pending the resolution of the prisoners' civil appeal before the supreme court, the instant court found that its authority to grant a stay of execution was limited by Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1001.1(C) (2011), and that although subsections (D), (E), and (F) referred to stays of execution, those subsections neither specified the conditions under which a stay could be granted nor specifically vest authority to do so; [2]-Although the state supreme court had the authority to deem an issue civil and so within its jurisdiction, it had no power to supersede a statute and manufacture jurisdiction for the prisoners' stay request by merely transferring the case to the instant court.


OUTCOME: Joint application for stay of execution denied.

Miller v. State


Case Number: D-2008-1206


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2013 OK CR 11; 313 P.3d 934; 2013 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 14



September 6, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Without prejudice, Motion granted by, Certificate of appealability denied Miller v. Trammell, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 103075 (N.D. Okla., Aug. 6, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DANA L. KUEHN, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Miller v. State, 2004 OK CR 29, 98 P.3d 738, 2004 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 32 (Okla. Crim. App., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because defendant was acquitted of the death penalty on the first count at his original trial, the death sentence on that count that was imposed in his second trial had to be reversed; [2]-Because a juror's answers regarding her willingness to consider the death penalty were equivocal, inconsistent, and confusing, the trial court erred in denying defense counsel any opportunity to question and attempt to rehabilitate her despite repeated requests from counsel to do so; [3]-The jury had more than enough evidence to conclude that defendant shot one victim and that he aided and abetted in the shooting of the second victim; [4]-One victim's stepmother should not have been allowed to testify as a victim impact witness on her own behalf because stepparents were not within the class of "immediate family" allowed to present such testimony under Okla. His death sentence on the second count was reversed and the case was remanded for resentencing. His applications for an evidentiary hearing were denied.

Johnson v. State

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion to suppress; the officer's initial stop of defendant was lawful because there was a reasonable possibility that the other traffic may have been affected by defendant's failure to use his turn signal, as required by Okla. Malone v. State


Case Number: D-2010-1084


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2013 OK CR 1; 293 P.3d 198; 2013 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 1



January 11, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Malone v. Oklahoma, 134 S. Ct. 172, 187 L. Ed. 2d 119, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 7028 (U.S., 2013)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Malone v. Trammell, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 150266 (W.D. Okla., Nov. 5, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMANCHE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE MARK R. SMITH, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Malone v. State, 2007 OK CR 34, 168 P.3d 185, 2007 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 33 (Okla. Crim. App., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Before defendant was resentenced for first degree murder, a newspaper article disclosed inadmissible evidence. Defendant said it was ineffective assistance for his counsel to then waive a sentencing jury. The appellate court disagreed because (1) counsel helped defendant make this strategic decision after a thorough investigation, (2) whether counsel used the best practice or common custom was not the applicable test, (3) an opinion poll of county residents did not control, (4) the trial court was not politically pressured, and (5) the trial judge could ignore inadmissible impact evidence.


OUTCOME: Sentence affirmed.

State v. Haworth

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The trial court abused its discretion by granting defendant's motion to quash charge of first-degree manslaughter under Okla. 216 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. State


Case Number: PCD-2004-321


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2012 OK CR 8; 281 P.3d 1283; 2012 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 6



April 5, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MCINTOSH COUNTY. THE HONORABLE THOMAS M. BARTHELD, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Murphy v. State, 2006 OK CR 3, 127 P.3d 1158, 2006 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 3 (Okla. Crim. App., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted for first degree murder and sentenced to death. On a second motion for post-conviction relief, a jury of the District Court of Mcintosh County, Oklahoma, found he was not mentally retarded. The trial court declared a mistrial and granted the State's motion to terminate further proceedings. Petitioner appealed the trial court's termination of the mental retardation proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The court held that Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 701.10b (Supp. 2006) was applicable to the remand determination of whether petitioner was mentally retarded, notwithstanding the statement by the court that § 701.10b(H) was not applicable during mandatory sentence review. Further, no plain error occurred under due process or Eighth Amendment principles when the district court granted the State's motion to terminate further proceedings. Petitioner received intelligence quotients of 80 and 82 on individually administered, scientifically recognized, standardized intelligence quotient tests and thus was not entitled to a jury trial on his claim of mental retardation. The court found that § 701.10b(C), disqualifying any defendant from being considered mentally retarded for the purpose of a sentence of death if that individual has received an intelligence quotient of 76 or above on any scientifically recognized intelligence quotient test, is constitutional. There was no violation of ex post facto principles, as the statute does not criminalize an act after the act has been committed and does not increase the severity of the crime or the punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that petitioner was not mentally retarded and denied his second application for post-conviction relief.

 

217 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hooley


Case Number: S-2010-1226


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2012 OK CR 3; 269 P.3d 949; 2012 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2



January 31, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OFOKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE GEARY L. WALKE, SPECIAL JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: In a case involving a charge of driving under the influence, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 11-902 (2001), the trial court erred in granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence based on an earlier determination in her license revocation case that her stop and seizure were unconstitutional because collateral estoppel did not apply. The District Attorney's Office and the Department of Public Safety were not the same parties for the purposes of collateral estoppel and the District Attorney's Office did not have a full and fair hearing on the search and seizure issue.


OUTCOME: Judgment granting motion to suppress reversed. Case remanded.

Coddington v. State


Case Number: D-2008-655


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2011 OK CR 17; 254 P.3d 684; 2011 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 18



May 13, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at, Motion denied by, Motion granted by Coddington v. State, 2011 OK CR 21, 259 P.3d 833, 2011 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 24 (Okla. Crim. App., 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Coddington v. Okla., 132 S. Ct. 588, 181 L. Ed. 2d 432, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 8252 (U.S., Nov. 14, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JERRY D. BASS, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Coddington v. State, 2006 OK CR 34, 142 P.3d 437, 2006 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 35 (Okla. Crim. App., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted sentenced him to death after he was convicted of first degree murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court violated his right to a fair and impartial jury by removing prospective jurors for cause over objection and absent proper questioning before it was adequately established that those jurors could not follow the law and consider the death penalty. As defendant had already been found guilty of first degree murder, the primary issue in jury selection was whether potential jurors could consider all three potential punishments. Defendant complained that the trial court removed 22 jurors for cause because the jurors were unable to consider imposing the death penalty, over his objection and without allowing him to rehabilitate the jurors. Of those 22 potential jurors, five were questioned as alternates. The court upheld the decision because defendant could not show prejudice from any alleged error that may have occurred when questioning the jurors because the record did not show that any alternate jurors sat on his jury. The court also held that it was harmless error when the trial judge left the bench during videotaped testimony that was offered in mitigation. The error was not structural in nature because there was no prejudice from the action.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

222 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Grissom v. State


Case Number: D-2008-595


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2011 OK CR 3; 253 P.3d 969; 2011 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 13



April 1, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Grissom v. Oklahoma, 132 S. Ct. 825, 181 L. Ed. 2d 534, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 8708 (U.S., 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by Grissom v. Duckworth, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 101688 (W.D. Okla., Aug. 3, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BLAINE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE RONALD G. FRANKLIN, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of Blaine County (Oklahoma) of first degree murder, shooting with intent to kill, grand larceny, and possession of a firearm after conviction of a felony. He was sentenced to death for first degree murder, imprisonment for life for shooting with intent to kill, twenty-five years for grand larceny, and forty years for possession of a firearm after former conviction of a felony. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the district court committed reversible error by failing to instruct the jury on the lesser-included offenses of second degree murder and first degree heat of passion or misdemeanor manslaughter and other lesser offenses applicable to the non-capital charges. The court of criminal appeals disagreed. Defendant's admission of guilt to the charges, through numerous statements of his counsel during trial, constituted a valid strategic election to present only a sentencing stage defense. By electing a sentencing stage defense, defendant foreclosed his claim to first-stage jury instructions on lesser-included offenses. The district court's failure to instruct the jury on lesser-included offenses did not "go to the foundation of the case" or take from the defendant any "right essential to his defense," and thus was not plain error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as modified.

 

223 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Harmon v. State


Case Number: D-2008-657


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2011 OK CR 6; 248 P.3d 918; 2011 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 5



January 27, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by, On rehearing at Harmon v. State, 2011 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 10 (Okla. Crim. App., Mar. 2, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Harmon v. Oklahoma, 565 U.S. 918, 132 S. Ct. 338, 181 L. Ed. 2d 211, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 5815 (2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Request denied by Harmon v. Royal, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 157091 (W.D. Okla., Nov. 14, 2016)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, that convicted him of first-degree felony murder under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(B) (2001), arguing that the district court erred in admitting the 911 recording into evidence and that imposition of the death sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment in violation of the Eighth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the trial court did not err in admitting the recording of the 911 call during the first stage of trial because it was admissible to corroborate witness testimony about the condition of the victim as well as the conversation had between the victim and the man who made the 911 call. Further, the victim's audible moans did not render the recording more prejudicial than probative under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2403 (Supp. 2002). The 911 tape was also properly admitted in the trial's second stage to support the aggravating circumstance that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel because it showed the victim's conscious physical suffering before his death; the fact that defendant did not contest the suffering of the victim did not make the recording more prejudicial than probative. The State had the burden to prove each aggravating circumstance beyond a reasonable doubt, and the 911 tape was convincing proof. Further, the court rejected defendant's argument that the imposition of the death sentence violated the ban against cruel and unusual punishment under the Eighth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

224 of 423 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of the 2010 Revisions


Case Number: CCAD-2011-1


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2011 OK CR 2; 2011 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 3



January 25, 2011, Decided 
January 25, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 31, 2011.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Oklahoma Court of Criminal Appeals Committee for Preparation of Uniform Jury Instructions submitted its report and recommendations for adoption of amendments to Oklahoma Uniform Jury Instructions-Criminal (Second Edition).


OVERVIEW: On review of the report by the committee and recommendations for the adoption of the 2010 proposed revisions to the Uniform Jury Instructions, the court accepted the report and concluded that the revisions should be adopted. As such, the court ordered that the proposed revisions were adopted, and the judges of the district court were directed to implement the utilization of the revisions effective immediately.


OUTCOME: The amendments were adopted and were to be implemented by the district courts.

 

225 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. State


Case Number: F-2009-836


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2010 OK CR 27; 252 P.3d 211; 2010 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 28



December 21, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF STEPHENS COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JOE H. ENOS, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Anderson v. State, 2010 OK CR 26, 252 P.3d 211, 2010 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 27 (Okla. Crim. App., 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Stephens County, Oklahoma, that convicted him of driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of drugs after a former conviction of two or more felonies under Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 11-902(A)(3) (Supp. 2006), arguing that the trial court's admission of evidence concerning the horizontal gaze nystagmus test was error because the State did not lay a proper foundation for its admissibility.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the trial court did not err in admitting the results of a Horizontal Gaze Nystagmus (HGN) test without scientific foundation by expert witnesses because the results, predicated by a proper foundation, were to be considered in the same manner as other field sobriety tests, such as the walk and turn test and the one-leg stand test. The testimony of the arresting deputies provided a proper foundation for the admission of the HGN, and the deputies were sufficiently qualified to administer the test. The testimony relating to the HGN test results was not offered as independent scientifically sound evidence of defendant's intoxication but was offered for the same purpose as other field sobriety test evidence--a physical act by defendant observed by the deputies contributing to the cumulative portrait of defendant as intoxicated in the deputies' opinions. Further, a scientific foundation for the test was not required because field sobriety tests were not based upon scientific evidence and were not a scientific test requiring scientific reliability. Therefore, neither Fry, Daubert, nor any other test establishing reliability or trustworthiness was applicable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

226 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


Case Number: F-2009-1140


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2010 OK CR 28; 250 P.3d 901; 2010 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 26



December 16, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL IN THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE VIRGIL BLACK, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, of first-degree rape under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1114 (Supp. 2008), forcible oral sodomy under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (Supp. 2007), and assault and battery by means likely to cause death under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 652 (Supp. 2007), arguing that the trial court erred in allowing the introduction of evidence that he previously raped and strangled a woman.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the the trial court did not abuse its discretion under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2413 (Supp. 2007), in allowing the State to introduce evidence of a rape of which defendant had previously been convicted in New Mexico and properly limited the evidence so that the jury would not learn that the victim of that prior rape was killed during the attack. The propensity evidence was probative to the charged offense because: (a) the sexual assaults were similar; (b) although six years elapsed between the rapes, defendant had been imprisoned for five of those years; (c) the record showed that the trial court, though not the jury, was aware that defendant had been accused of similar rapes accompanied by strangulation in 1988 and in July 2008, shortly before the crime for which defendant was presently being tried; (d) the record suggested no intervening events beyond defendant's prison term and move to Oklahoma; (e) as the New Mexico victim could not testify, the State called three witnesses, each of whom testified about a limited and specific area of the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Burgess v. State


Case Number: F-2009-308


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2010 OK CR 25; 243 P.3d 461; 2010 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 25



November 16, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Burgess v. Evans, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 169478 (W.D. Okla., Nov. 3, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MAJOR COUNTY. THE HONORABLE N. VINSON BAREFOOT, ASSOCIATE DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the District Court of Major County, Oklahoma, of engaging in a pattern of criminal offenses under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 425 (Supp. 2004); bribery by a public official under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 382 (2001); kidnapping under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 741 (Supp. 2004); forcible oral sodomy under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 888(B) (Supp. 2006); and second-degree rape under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 1111 (Supp. 2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a county sheriff and was part of a district court's drug court team. Further, because the evidence supported a finding the victim was under the legal custody or supervision of a political subdivision of the State and that defendant was an employee of the political subdivision that exercised authority over her, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Cuesta-Rodriguez v. State


Case Number: D-2007-825


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2010 OK CR 23; 241 P.3d 214; 2010 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 23



October 12, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, Motion denied by Cuesta-Rodriguez v. State, 2011 OK CR 4, 247 P.3d 1192, 2011 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 4 (Okla. Crim. App., 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Cuesta-Rodriguez v. Oklahoma, 565 U.S. 885, 132 S. Ct. 259, 181 L. Ed. 2d 151, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 5267 (2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by, Judgment entered by Cuesta-Rodriguez v. Royal, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 134416 (W.D. Okla., Sept. 29, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE VIRGIL C. BLACK, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, that convicted him of first-degree murder under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 701.7 (2001), arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction because evidence of his intent to kill the victim was insufficient to overcome evidence that he was intoxicated and thus unable to form the specific intent to kill.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's murder conviction for killing his girlfriend because the victim's adult daughter witnessed defendant shoot the victim in the face, defendant admitted to the police that he shot the victim, and defendant was the only person in the house with the victim when the police arrived and heard her screams stop when a second gunshot was heard. Testimony from a firearms examiner showed that the handgun defendant used was unusual in that it required several sequential steps to be fired a second time, and after he shot the victim the second time, defendant remained barricaded in the house, even though there were police and emergency medical personnel just outside that could have aided the victim. When the evidence was considered in the light most favorable to the State, it was sufficient to permit a rational trier of fact to conclude that defendant intended to kill the victim with either the first or second gunshot despite some evidence showing that he was intoxicated but not so intoxicated that his mental powers were overcome rendering him incapable of forming criminal intent.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and the trial court's imposition of the death penalty were affirmed.

Mitchell v. State


Case Number: D-2008-57


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2010 OK CR 14; 235 P.3d 640; 2010 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 13



July 1, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Mitchell v. Oklahoma, 562 U.S. 1293, 131 S. Ct. 1688, 179 L. Ed. 2d 627, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 2295 (2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by Mitchell v. Duckworth, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 97980 (W.D. Okla., July 27, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE VIRGIL C. BLACK, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Mitchell v. State, 2006 OK CR 20, 136 P.3d 671, 2006 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 22 (Okla. Crim. App., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the capital sentenced imposed by the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, following his second re-sentencing trial, arguing that crime scene photographs were improperly admitted in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2403 (2001), and that the evidence was insufficient to support the finding of an aggravator factor under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.12(4) (1991).


OVERVIEW: At defendant's second re-sentencing trial, the jury found the existence of the aggravating circumstance that the murder was committed in an especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel manner under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.12(4), and recommended imposition of the death sentence. The district court accepted the jury's recommendation and imposed a capital sentence. On review, the court held that photographs of the deceased and crime scene were properly admitted because they proved the existence of the "heinous, atrocious or cruel" aggravator. Further, the court rejected defendant's argument that the evidence was insufficient to support the finding of the especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravating factor because the evidence on this issue was profoundly compelling. The properly admitted evidence overwhelmingly established that defendant inflicted serious physical abuse inflicted upon his victim in attempting to rape her that resulted in conscious physical suffering by the victim until defendant delivered the final crushing blows with a coat rack that pierced the victim's skull and ended her life.


OUTCOME: The sentence of death was affirmed.

Goode v. State


Case Number: D-2008-43


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2010 OK CR 10; 236 P.3d 671; 2010 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 11



June 9, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Goode v. Oklahoma, 562 U.S. 1231, 131 S. Ct. 1497, 179 L. Ed. 2d 326, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 1525 (2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied, Sub nomine at Johnson v. Province, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 48813 (N.D. Okla., Apr. 4, 2013)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by, Certificate of appealability granted Goode v. Duckworth, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 89319 (N.D. Okla., July 11, 2016)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, that convicted him of three counts of first-degree murder, with alternative theories of malice or felony murder, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (Supp. 2004), and one count of first-degree burglary in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1431 (2001), and that sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two accomplices broke into a home and killed all three people inside, a husband and wife and their 10-year-old daughter. Following his convictions, the trial court imposed a capital sentence. On review, the court held that the trial court did not err in admitting a witness statement in its entirety. Under the rule of completeness, codified at Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2107 (Supp. 2002), a party that introduced part of a statement could not object when the adverse party sought to introduce the previously unintroduced portion. Further, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the testimony of a fellow inmate that defendant admitted to committing the murders because evidence that a defendant relayed details of a crime that only the perpetrator could have known was relevant evidence. In addition, in light of the heinous nature of the crime committed, the evidence was sufficient to support the finding of the continuing threat aggravator under 21 Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.12(7) (2001), to justify the capital sentence imposed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and capital sentence were affirmed.

Randolph v. State


Case Number: F-2008-208


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2010 OK CR 2; 231 P.3d 672; 2010 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2



February 4, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied, Stay denied by, As moot Randolph v. Chester, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 180134 (N.D. Okla., Dec. 20, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JESSE S. HARRIS, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, defendant was found guilty of trafficking in illegal drugs, Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-415 (Supp. 2004); possession of marijuana, second offense, Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-402 (Supp. 2004); and failure to obtain a drug tax stamp, Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 450.3 (2001), and was sentenced to, among other things, life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The police received a tip regarding the sale of drugs in an apartment; the officers testified that the person who answered the apartment door consented to a search and voluntarily signed the search warrant waiver and consent form. The officer observed defendant near a bedroom and found drugs on defendant. The court disagreed with defendant's argument that this trial was barred by former jeopardy. During the previous trial, defendant's counsel consistently turned down the trial judge's offer to declare a mistrial for the impermissible injection of evidentiary harpoons, Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2403 (2004). When an experienced trial court concluded that defendant's rights to a fair and impartial trial and effective assistance of counsel were irreparably compromised, it was faced with a cogent and compelling reason to order a mistrial and discharge the jury. There was no abuse of discretion in this ruling and no former acquittal which barred defendant's retrial and conviction. The officers were in the apartment based on a co-inhabitant's consent and plainly viewed defendant in possession of drugs. Therefore, there was no unreasonable search and seizure, Okla. Const. art. II, § 30.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

232 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Collins v. State


Case Number: F-2008-654


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2009 OK CR 32; 223 P.3d 1014; 2009 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 32



December 17, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Collins v. State, 2016 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 25 (Okla. Crim. App., June 29, 2016)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Collins v. Bear, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 121551 (W.D. Okla., Aug. 22, 2016)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of an Oklahoma trial court that convicted him of two counts of first-degree rape under Okla. Stat. art. 21, §§ 1111 and 1114 (Supp. 2006) and two counts of kidnapping under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 741 (Supp. 2004), arguing that the joinder of the charges against him in a single trial was erroneous and that the trial court erred in precluding him from impeaching a victim regarding her history of prostitution.


OVERVIEW: In two separate instances, each victim agreed to go somewhere with defendant in his car but were instead brought to his home, where they were attacked and raped. Although the instances occurred one week apart, charges stemming from both incidents were joined. On review, the court held that the charges were properly joined because both encounters displayed defendant's unique predatory pattern and common plan of attack and because evidence of the pattern and common plan was relevant to proving both kidnappings and both rapes. Further, the trial court did not err in precluding defendant from impeaching one of the victim's regarding her history of prostitution. Prior convictions under Okla. Stat. art. 12, § 2609(A) (Supp. 2004), were admissible if they involved dishonesty, and Okla. Stat. art. 12, § 2609(B) did not make crimes regarding moral turpitude, by themselves, generally admissible for impeachment purposes. Further, Oklahoma's rape shield statute, Okla. Stat. art. 12, § 2412 (2001), contained no exception allowing for a complainant's history of prostitution, either acts or convictions, to be brought out at trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Sanchez v. State


Case Number: D-2006-627


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2009 OK CR 31; 223 P.3d 980; 2009 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 31



December 14, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Sanchez v. Oklahoma, 562 U.S. 931, 131 S. Ct. 326, 178 L. Ed. 2d 212, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 7658 (Oct. 4, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Sanchez v. Trammell, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 18544 (W.D. Okla., Feb. 17, 2015)
Post-conviction relief denied at Sanchez v. State, 2017 OK CR 22, 2017 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 20 (Okla. Crim. App., Aug. 22, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CLEVELAND COUNTY. THE HONORABLE WILLIAM C. HETHERINGTON, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Cleveland County, Oklahoma, that convicted him of first-degree murder under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (Supp. 1996), first-degree rape under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1114(A)(3) (1991), and forcible sodomy under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 888(B)(3) (Supp. 1992) and that imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the district erred under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 15 (2001), in acquiescing to the request of law enforcement personnel that defendant be shackled because the statute required a factual predicate sufficient to justify the restraint and no showing was made. However, because care was taken to conceal the restraints and no juror observed them, defendant suffered no prejudice. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions because it tended to show that defendant forced the victim into her car, sexually assaulted her, murdered her, dumped her body, and took some of her belongings with him where DNA evidence extracted from sperm was found in the vehicle, on the victim, and on her clothing, where phone calls made from the victim's phone after her murder were placed to defendant's then-girlfriend, and where footprints of a Nike tread pattern were found at the scene and defendant owned shoes with the same tread pattern and of the same size. After reviewing the evidence and finding that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating evidence, the court concluded that the sentence of death was factually supported and appropriate.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the imposition of a capital sentence were affirmed.

K. M. C. v. State


Case Number: J-2009-258


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile appealed the order of the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, granting the State's motion to sentence appellant as an adult.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged as a youthful offender with assault and battery with a deadly weapon, attempted robbery with a firearm, and first degree burglary. Appellant was seventeen years old. 235 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Love v. State


Case Number: F-2008-236


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2009 OK CR 20; 217 P.3d 116; 2009 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 19



June 30, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Love v. Parker, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 48815 (N.D. Okla., Apr. 4, 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) of trafficking in controlled drugs under Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-415 (Supp. 2004). He was sentenced to 20 years in prison and a fine of $ 25,000, all but $ 500 suspended. The judgment showed that he convicted after conviction of a prior offense. Defendant appealed. He was also convicted in non-jury proceedings of failure to signal under Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 11-604 (2001).


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised various issues on appeal, but the court affirmed. Defendant could not waive his right to a jury trial without the consent of the State. Although defendant attempted to waive a jury trial, he had no right to unilaterally waive jury assessment of punishment. Any rational trier of fact could have found that defendant failed to signal before turning and that failure might have affected other traffic, which supported his conviction in this regard. An officer testified that he saw defendant turn without signaling and there was no opposing testimony. Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-415 (Supp. 2004) did not presume that trafficking defendants were major drug dealers. The court rejected defendant's claim that the statute violated due process. To prove his equal protection claim, defendant had to show that Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-415 (Supp. 2004) interfered with his exercise of a fundamental right or operated to his disadvantage as a member of a suspect class, or show that the statute was not rationally related to a legitimate state interest. Treating some differently by the enactment of the trafficking statute does not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence was affirmed. The case was remanded for an order nunc pro tunc correcting the judgment and sentence to reflect that defendant was not convicted after conviction of a prior offense. The mandate was ordered issued upon the delivery and filing of this decision.

Magnan v. State


Case Number: D-2005-683


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2009 OK CR 16; 207 P.3d 397; 2009 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 13



April 22, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Magnan v. Oklahoma, 558 U.S. 906, 130 S. Ct. 276, 175 L. Ed. 2d 185, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 5819 (Oct. 5, 2009)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by Magnan v. Trammell, 719 F.3d 1159, 2013 U.S. App. LEXIS 12410 (10th Cir. Okla., June 14, 2013)
Related proceeding at, Motion denied by United States v. Magnan, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 54929 (E.D. Okla., Apr. 21, 2014)
Appeal dismissed by, Motion granted by United States v. Magnan, 2017 U.S. App. LEXIS 13096 (10th Cir., July 20, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SEMINOLE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE GEORGE BUTNER, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Seminole County (Oklahoma) convicting him for three counts of first degree murder, under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 701.7 (2001), and one count of shooting with intent to kill, in violation of Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 652 (2001). Defendant was sentenced to death on each of the murder counts and to a term of life imprisonment on the shooting count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant waived his right to a direct appeal, stated that he had nothing to present in mitigation, and requested a death sentence. On a mandatory sentence review for all death-penalty cases, pursuant to Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 701.13 (2001) and Okla. R. Ct. Crim. App. 9.4, the court considered whether the crimes occurred in Indian County such that the State lacked jurisdiction. The murders occurred in a house located on property that was part of the original restricted allotment of a full-blooded Seminole, and 4/5ths of the surface interests in the property remained restricted against alienation as Indian land. The court held that the State's interest in exercising criminal jurisdiction over the property overwhelmed any fractional interest any Indian heirs of the original allottee might own in the unseen mineral estate. The court found that the sentence imposed was based upon aggravated circumstances that were supported by the evidence and were not under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor, pursuant to the sentence review procedure under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 701.12. Defendant had an opportunity to present mitigating evidence and chose not to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

Rojem v. State


Case Number: D-2007-660


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2009 OK CR 15; 207 P.3d 385; 2009 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 15



April 15, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rojem v. Oklahoma, 130 S. Ct. 1065, 175 L. Ed. 2d 897, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 307 (U.S., 2010)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Appeal dismissed by, Motion denied by, As moot Rojem v. Workman, 2011 U.S. App. LEXIS 17547 (10th Cir. Okla., Aug. 23, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WASHITA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE CHARLES L. GOODWIN, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Rojem v. State, 1988 OK CR 57, 753 P.2d 359, 1988 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 55 (Okla. Crim. App., 1988)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the District Court of Washita County (Oklahoma), which sentenced him to death after he was convicted of first-degree murder. He was also convicted of kidnapping and rape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried by a jury and convicted of kidnapping, rape and first degree murder. He currently appealed from his sentence of death, but the appellate court affirmed. Two panelists initially expressed reservations about aspects of capital punishment that would have cat doubt on their fitness for jury service. However, each panelist said that she was able to consider all of the evidence presented and give meaningful and fair consideration to all three punishments. Therefore, the trial court did not err in denying the challenges for cause. While the trial court abused its discretion in refusing to allow defendant's expert witness to use demonstrative aids during his testimony, witnesses were able to present a great deal of information regarding defendant's development and factors related to his ability to make good decisions. The record showed that jurors were able to use that information in their deliberations. The death penalty was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor. Sufficient evidence supported the aggravating circumstances and no improper evidence or argument was admitted that could have unfairly swayed the jury's decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Grant v. State


Case Number: D-2006-14


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2009 OK CR 11; 205 P.3d 1; 2009 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 11



March 23, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Grant v. Oklahoma, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 7370 (U.S., Oct. 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JERRY D. BASS, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) convicting him for two counts of first degree, malice aforethought murder, under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (2001), and two counts of robbery with firearms, under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 801 (2001). The jury recommended punishment of death on the murder counts and life sentences on the robbery counts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed two employees of a hotel and took money from the hotel register and from the purse of one of the victims. Defendant first contended that he was incompetent to stand trial due to a mental illness. The court held that defendant was competent under the standards of Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1175.1 (2005) because there was no reason to second-guess the judgments of defense counsel, the trial court, and the defense experts that determined that defendant was competent at the time of his trial. Where defendant wrote a letter indicating that he wished to be relieved of counsel several weeks before trial and where the trial court failed to conduct a hearing on his request, the record did not support a conclusion that defendant made a clear, unequivocal expression of the desire to waive the assistance of counsel and to proceed pro se. Defendant was not denied a fair trial regarding the composition of the jury. The robberies had a sufficient separation of time and place to justify the two convictions and did not violate double jeopardy principles, under U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV, and Okla. Const. art. 2, § 21. The court also found no errors in the capital punishment stage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentences of the district court.

James v. State


Case Number: F-2007-1052


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2009 OK CR 8; 204 P.3d 793; 2009 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 8



March 6, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by James v. Oklahoma, 558 U.S. 944, 130 S. Ct. 441, 175 L. Ed. 2d 266, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 7383 (2009)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part James v. Standifird, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 164300 (N.D. Okla., Nov. 19, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE THOMAS C. GILLERT, DISTRICT JUDGE.
James v. State, 2007 OK CR 1, 152 P.3d 255, 2007 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 1 (Okla. Crim. App., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, that convicted him of rape by instrumentation under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 1111 (2001) and lewd molestation under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 1123 (2002), arguing that the trial court erred in permitting his former stepdaughter to testify that he had sexually abused her years earlier.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with sexually abusing a four-year-old girl. The girl, who was nine at the time of trial, testified that defendant placed his finger in her vagina and his penis in her mouth and had ejaculated in her mouth on more than one occasion. The State also presented testimony from defendant's former stepdaughter, who testified that defendant had abused her in the same manner. On review of defendant's convictions, the court held that the trial court did not err in admitting the testimony of his former stepdaughter. The mere fact that retroactively-applied evidentiary laws Okla. Stat. art. 12, § 2413 (2007), and Okla. Stat. art. 12, § 2414 (2007), worked to defendant's disadvantage did not mean that the laws were ex post facto. Further, the testimony of defendant's former stepdaughter was admissible under these statutes because the particulars of the prior crime showed a visible connection to the instant charge and demonstrated a common scheme to take advantage of very young girls. Both the instant offense and the past offense involved girls about the same age, and the girls gave contemporaneous descriptions of defendant's conduct that were eerily similar to each other.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

240 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Horn v. State


Case Number: F-2007-1240


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2009 OK CR 7; 204 P.3d 777; 2009 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 9



March 6, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE PATRICIA G. PARRISH, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, that convicted him of rape under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1114 (1991), and forcible oral sodomy under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 888 (Supp. 1992), arguing that the trial court erred in admitting propensity evidence under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2413 (Supp. 2007), and that the statute of limitations, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 152 (1994), barred his prosecution.


OVERVIEW: In defendant's trial for the sexual abuse of his stepdaughter, the trial court permitted a witness with whom defendant has consensual sex to testify to statements defendant made regarding his sexual preferences. On review, the court held that the propensity evidence was admissible under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2413 (Supp. 2007), and that the statute did not violate due process or equal protection concerns. The introduction of prior acts evidence was limited by Okla. Stat. tit. 12 Okla. Stat. tit. 12, §§ 2402 and 2403 (2001), which ensured that such evidence would not be admitted if its prejudicial effect outweighed its probative value. Sex crimes were crimes of propensity, and the need for corroborating evidence in cases of child sexual abuse due to the highly secretive nature of the crime justified the admission of prior crimes evidence. Further, the statute of limitations did not bar prosecution. Although more than seven years had passed since the commission of the offenses, the victim told no one about the crimes because she was afraid of defendant, who had been a police officer. While she remained silent about defendant's sexual abuse, the statute of limitations was tolled.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Jones v. State


Case Number: D-2005-599


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2009 OK CR 1; 201 P.3d 869; 2009 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2



January 21, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Jones v. Oklahoma, 558 U.S. 895, 130 S. Ct. 237, 175 L. Ed. 2d 163, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 5846 (2009)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part, As moot Jones v. Workman, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 45186 (W.D. Okla., Apr. 7, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE SUSAN P. CASWELL, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) convicting him of three counts of first-degree malice murder under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 701.7(A) (2001) and two counts of shooting with intent to kill under Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 652 (2001) and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for shooting the five victims, killing three of them. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by failing to remove a prospective juror who had expressed reservations "about how you shoot five people in self-defense" under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 659(2) (2001) because the court did not find that the trial court improperly persuaded the juror into saying that she could be a fair juror. Given her responses throughout voir dire, the court was left with the impression that if the juror felt that she could not be a fair juror, she would have said so. The trial court did not err by failing to excuse a lieutenant in a city police department under Okla. Stat. tit. 38, § 28(B)(4) because the statute did not apply to all law enforcement officers and the lieutenant did not have any experience as a jailor or having custody of prisoners. The trial court did not err by failing to sua sponte striking the lieutenant for cause under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 659(2) (2001) on the ground that 23 years earlier he had worked with one of the prosecutors, he was acquainted with the police officers, and he supervised one of the officers on the witness list.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Hall


Case Number: S-2007-19 2


2 The following appellate cases were consolidated into the current appeal under Case No. S-2007-19: State v. James Leroy Patton, S-2007-20; State v. Donald R. Hall, S-2007-21, S-2007-22 and S-2007-106; State v. Michael Ray Hall, S-2007-23; State v Eldon W. McCumber, Donald Hall, Michael Ray Hall, James Leroy Patton, Kenneth L. Doughty, Michael S. Chaloner and William Sparks, S-2007-107.


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2008 OK CR 15; 185 P.3d 397; 2008 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 15



May 23, 2008, Decided 
May 23, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE ROMA M. MCELWEE, SPECIAL JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, the State challenged the order of the Oklahoma County District Court, Oklahoma, quashing the grand jury indictments brought against defendants and suppressing evidence taken by the multicounty grand jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendants alleged the presence of two alternate jurors in the grand jury room while evidence was being taken violated of Okla. Const. art. II, § 18 and Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 340(C) (2001). The State argued that the presence of alternate jurors in the grand jury proceedings during the reception of evidence was authorized by Okla. Stat. tit. 38, § 21 (Supp. 2004). In a plurality opinion, the court ruled that Okla. Stat. tit. 38, § 21 was constitutional and the presence of the alternate grand jurors in the grand jury room and their participation during the evidentiary phase of the proceedings was proper. By reading Okla. Stat. tit. 22 § 340(C) and Okla. Stat. tit. 38, § 21 together it was clear that the Oklahoma Legislature intentionally expanded the list of who could be present in the grand jury room during its proceedings to include alternate jurors. Alternate grand jurors provided by Okla. Stat. tit. 38, § 21 were fully compatible with Okla. Const. art. II, § 18, and there was no limitation on the number of persons who could be qualified as alternate grand or petit jurors in anticipation of exercising fact-finding powers if a regular juror was unable to do so.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and remanded to the district court for a preliminary hearing.

 

243 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Durant v. State


Case Number: F-2007-164


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2008 OK CR 17; 188 P.3d 192; 2008 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 14



May 23, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE TWYLA MASON GRAY, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, convicted defendant, after a bench trial, of taking clandestine photographs, under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1171(B) (2001), after conviction of a felony. The trial court sentenced defendant to six years in prison, provided that on successful completion of certain behavioral programs, the balance of the sentence would have been suspended. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence presented at the bench trial showed that defendant had used a digital camera, hidden in a backpack, to take photographs of a female student in the lobby of a community college without her knowledge. The evidence supported a conclusion that defendant had intentionally tried to position the backpack so that the camera, nestled inside an open compartment of the pack, would have captured images of the student's body underneath her skirt. Defendant claimed that any attempt to clandestinely photograph any part of a person, while the person was in a public place, was not a crime under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1171(B) (2001). The plain language of § 1171(B) referred to one's reasonable expectation of privacy while "in" a particular place, not to one's expectations about a particular place "on" one's body. The court did not believe that § 1171(B) covered the clandestine taking of photographs of a person who was in a public place, regardless of what part of the body the perpetrator focused on. Accordingly, defendant's conviction must have been reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment and the sentence of the district court was reversed.

 

244 of 423 DOCUMENTS


M.A.W. v. State


Case Number: J-2007-955


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2008 OK CR 16; 185 P.3d 388; 2008 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 13



May 20, 2008, Decided 
May 20, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE D. FRED DOAK, SPECIAL JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of an order from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which denied his motion for youthful offender status after he was charged with first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was charged as an adult with first-degree murder. The alleged crime occurred when the juvenile was 17 years old. The juvenile sought certification to be tried as a youthful offender or a juvenile. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the juvenile claimed that a bill enacted in 2007 revising the Oklahoma Youthful Offender Act provisions then codified at Okla. Stat. tit. 10, §§ 7306-2.2 and 7306-2.5 (Supp. 2006) was unconstitutional because it was passed in violation of the anti-logrolling and single-subject provisions of Okla. Const. art. 5, § 57. The court found that the bill was a valid legislative enactment under art. 5, § 57 as a bill adopting a revision of statutes. The Oklahoma Legislature intended, through the bill, only to revise duplicate bills, which amended the same sections of the Youthful Offender Act in order to merge them and to reconcile any conflicts therein. The trial court properly denied the juvenile's motion for youthful offender status based on Okla. Stat. tit. 10, §§ 7306-2.2 and 7306-2.5 ( Supp. 2007). The statutes were not unconstitutionally overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

245 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Ochoa v. Bass


Case Number: HC-2007-1120


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2008 OK CR 11; 181 P.3d 727; 2008 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 8



March 12, 2008, Decided 
March 12, 2008, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought writs of habeas corpus and prohibition in connection with orders issued by respondent district court judge requiring petitioners to be taken into custody by respondent sheriff in Oklahoma County District Court (Oklahoma).


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, Spanish-speaking defendants in criminal matters, were in court to be sentenced for unrelated charges when the judge asked them about their legal status in the country. Their answers led him to order petitioners committed to the custody of the sheriff. The judge relied on House Bill 1804, the Oklahoma Taxpayer and Citizen Protection Act of 2007, 2007 Okla. Sess. Laws ch. 112, § 1, at 546, which he believed required him to notify the sheriff of persons illegally in the country. The court found that House Bill 1804 did not authorize petitioners' commitment. However, under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 201 (2001), giving the judge power to command the arrest of a person when an offense was committed in his presence, the judge could lawfully order the sheriff to take custody of petitioners. The court also found that the judge had legal authority to question petitioners regarding their immigration status during the sentencing hearing. However, under 8 C.F.R. § 287.7(d) (2007), petitioners were required to be released once the Bureau of Immigration and Customs Enforcement failed to take any action against petitioners within 48 hours of detainer notices.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writs of prohibition but issued writs of habeas corpus ordering petitioners released from custody.

Rochon v. State


Case Number: F-2006-971


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2008 OK CR 1; 176 P.3d 362; 2008 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 1



January 8, 2008, Decided 
January 8, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE GORDON D. MCALLISTER, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, sentencing him to fifteen years for trafficking in illegal drugs, eight years for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute, a fine for failure to obtain a tax stamp, and one year for unlawful possession of paraphernalia, with the sentences to run consecutively.


OVERVIEW: The police were preparing to execute a search warrant at a residence, and observed defendant and another male leave the house and drive away in defendant's car. The vehicle was stopped for a traffic violation. Defendant was arrested and returned to the residence where he remained until the search was completed. At the residence, police executing the warrant found 326.5 grams of methamphetamine and approximately twenty pounds of marijuana in a safe in defendant's bedroom. After he was Mirandized, defendant admitted he had been selling drugs for about six months, and stated that he sold approximately four pounds of methamphetamine and twenty pounds of marijuana a week. The appellate court ruled that while the police used a traffic violation to justify the stop in the case, such was not necessary to detain defendant while his residence was being searched pursuant to a lawful search warrant for contraband based upon a finding of probable cause. The police sought to detain defendant while they executed a lawful warrant to search his home for contraband. Although defendant was stopped about a mile from his home, this was, under the circumstances, as soon as practicable.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute was reversed with instructions to dismiss, and the judgment and sentences were otherwise affirmed.

 

247 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Autry v. State


Case Number: M-2005-7


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2007 OK CR 41; 172 P.3d 212; 2007 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 40



November 2, 2007, Decided 
November 2, 2007, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an attorney, was held in direct contempt of court, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 565.1 (2001) in the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma). The matter was transferred to another district judge who, after a hearing, found defendant in direct contempt and ordered him to pay a fine, plus the amount of costs to the State resulting from his conduct. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant represented a client whose conviction had been reversed on appeal. Defendant believed that certain evidence was admissible at trial; however, the trial judge ruled that the evidence was inadmissible. Before the jury, nevertheless, defendant made reference to the inadmissible evidence. The dispositive question before the appellate court was whether defendant's conduct constituted direct contempt of court under the circumstances presented here. That was a question of law and appellate review was de novo. That the district court's order in the case could have been wrong was simply not relevant. Wrong or not, it was the order of the district court. Further, the appellate court determined that the statement to the jury was neither a slip of the tongue, nor an outburst made in an unguarded moment of passion. It was made in cool, calculated, contemptuous defiance of the district court's authority and with full awareness of the potential consequences. Moreover, defendant's conduct was not tempered as client zealous advocacy. To defy the district court's order in front of the jury was simply bad behavior and direct contempt of court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court in finding the defendant guilty of direct contempt was affirmed. The fine was also affirmed; however, the order directing payment of costs was set aside and held for naught.

Malone v. State


Case Number: D-2005-600


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2007 OK CR 34; 168 P.3d 185; 2007 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 33



August 31, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Malone v. State, 2013 OK CR 1, 2013 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 1 (Okla. Crim. App., 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMANCHE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE MARK R. SMITH, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Comanche County (Oklahoma) convicting him of first-degree malice aforethought murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for shooting the victim, a highway patrol trooper, to death while the trooper was attempting to arrest defendant for manufacturing methamphetamine in his car. On appeal, the court held that even though the jury instructions concerning the defense of voluntary intoxication were incorrect, the error was harmless because the evidence against defendant was overwhelming and clearly established that defendant knew what he was doing and deliberately chose to shoot and kill the victim. However, the court held that the trial court abused its discretion by failing to constrain the amount and content of the victim impact evidence presented during sentencing, erred by failing to hold a hearing on the admissibility of the evidence, and defense counsel was ineffective for failing to challenge the evidence. The error was not harmless because, while defendant might have only had a slim chance of avoiding a death sentence, the religious and duty-based plea of the victim's wife that defendant be shown no mercy squelched whatever slim chance he had. The overall victim impact evidence was too long and too emotional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but his sentence was reversed and the case was remanded to the district court for resentencing.

Harris v. State


Case Number: PCD-2005-665


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2007 OK CR 32; 167 P.3d 438; 2007 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 32



August 20, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Harris v. State, 2004 OK CR 1, 84 P.3d 731, 2004 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2 (Okla. Crim. App., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner's death sentence for first degree murder was reversed on appeal and remanded for resentencing. On remand, the jury found that the petitioner knowingly created a great risk of death to more than one person, and constituted a continuing threat to society. The judge from the Oklahoma trial court imposed the death penalty, which was affirmed on appeal. The petitioner filed an application for capital post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: In his application for capital post-conviction relief, the petitioner raised several issues contending trial and resentencing appellate counsel were all ineffective. In making these claims, he alleged trial counsel was ineffective in several instances and appellate counsel was ineffective for not raising these claims. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that the petitioner offered examples of ineffective assistance of counsel, either by counsel, appellate counsel, or both. Insofar as the petitioner intended to separately raise claims of ineffective assistance of trial counsel at the first trial, the appellate court denied those claims. In reference to several of the petitioner's other claims, he failed to show the alleged acts of ineffectiveness prejudiced him; these included claims that some of the prosecutor's statements to the jury were improper, and claims that certain evidence seized by the State should have been found by counsel. Contrary to the petitioner's assertions, he was not tried while in restraints; thus, appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to claim that trial counsel was ineffective by allowing the jury to see the petitioner in restraints.


OUTCOME: The application for capital post-conviction relief, motion for evidentiary hearing, motion for discovery, and motion to supplement application were denied.

Harris v. State


Case Number: D-2005-117


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2007 OK CR 28; 164 P.3d 1103; 2007 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 28



July 19, 2007, Decided 
July 19, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Harris v. Oklahoma, 552 U.S. 1286, 128 S. Ct. 1717, 170 L. Ed. 2d 524, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2789 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE VIRGIL C. BLACK, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Harris v. State, 2004 OK CR 1, 84 P.3d 731, 2004 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2 (Okla. Crim. App., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (2001). On remand, a jury at defendant's resentencing trial found that defendant knowingly created a great risk of death to more than one person and constituted a continuing threat to society. In accordance with the jury's recommendation, the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) imposed the death penalty. Defendant appealed the sentence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not plainly err in failing to use the recommended instructions on jury note-taking where it told jurors that notes were for their personal use only and otherwise properly instructed the jury. The failure to provide a complete record of the sentence proceedings did not violate defendant's constitutional rights where the record was complete enough for the appellate court to evaluate the jury's verdict. The evidence was sufficient to support the jury's finding on the continuing threat aggravating circumstance where the evidence showed that defendant had a lifelong pattern of using violence that was likely to continue. Okla. Stat. tit. 21, §§ 12.1 and 13.1 (2001), did not apply as defendant's crimes were committed prior to March 1, 2000. The initial prosecutorial argument that the jury should not consider mitigating evidence was harmless where the jury was properly instructed as to the consideration of mitigating evidence. The claims of ineffective assistance of counsel failed as defendant was not prejudiced by counsel's failure to, inter alia, seek a determination that he was mentally retarded or to present evidence of his diminished mental capacity.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

Case Number: D-2004-1260


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2007 OK CR 27; 164 P.3d 1089; 2007 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 27



July 11, 2007, Decided 
July 11, 2007, Filed

Writ of habeas corpus denied, Request denied by, Certificate of appealability granted, in part Cole v. Workman, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 99042 (N.D. Okla., Sept. 1, 2011)
Related proceeding at Warner v. Gross, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 196241 (W.D. Okla., Dec. 12, 2014)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Stay granted by Cole v. Trammell, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 88412 (N.D. Okla., July 8, 2015)
Writ denied by, Stay denied by, As moot Cole v. Trammell, 2015 OK CR 13, 358 P.3d 932, 2015 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 12 (Okla. Crim. App., Oct. 2, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF ROGERS COUNTY. THE HONORABLE J. DWAYNE STEIDLEY, ASSOCIATE DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the District Court of Rogers County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first-degree murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 707.1(C) (Supp. 2001). He was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of his first-degree murder conviction, but the appellate court affirmed. The victim was his nine-month old daughter. He had tried to get her to stop crying, grabbed her by the ankles, and pushed her legs toward her head until she flipped over. The action broke the child's back and resulted in fatal injuries. The denial of defendant's motion for continuance 12 days before trial was proper because the decision to cut off the window of opportunity for developing even better evidence did not amount to an abuse of discretion. Moreover, there was no ineffective assistance of trial counsel with respect to the way the defense team handled the issue and no prejudice, as no evidence had apparently been developed in the two years since defendant's trial occurred. His prior criminal conviction and prison sentence in California for aggravated child abuse was appropriately admitted because that evidence was inextricably intertwined with the State's investigation of the current case and connected to its burden of proof. More importantly, some of the evidence went to intent, an exception found in Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2404(B) (2001).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Pavatt v. State


Case Number: D-2003-1186


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2007 OK CR 19; 159 P.3d 272; 2007 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 19



May 8, 2007, Decided  
May 8, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Related proceeding at Andrew v. State, 2007 OK CR 23, 164 P.3d 176, 2007 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 25 (Okla. Crim. App., 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Pavatt v. Oklahoma, 552 U.S. 1181, 128 S. Ct. 1229, 170 L. Ed. 2d 62, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 1358 (2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by Pavatt v. Trammell, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 60527 (W.D. Okla., May 1, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) convicting him of first-degree murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 421 and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his co-defendant were convicted for shooting the victim, the co-defendant's husband, to death. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion for a change of venue based on pretrial publicity because defendant did not show that any juror actually seated was biased against him due to adverse pretrial publicity; the trial court excused a number of prospective jurors who admitted that pretrial publicity had affected their ability to be impartial. Defendant's convictions for both first-degree murder and conspiracy to commit murder did not violate the prohibitions against double jeopardy or the prohibition against double punishment of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 11 (2001) because the fact that evidence of a plan to profit financially from the victim's murder was relevant to both the conspiracy charge and the murder for remuneration aggravating circumstance supporting the death penalty for the murder charge did not offend double jeopardy principles. The murder, and the plan to commit it, were not the same act as contemplated by § 11 as neither crime was an indispensable part of the other.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.
