Murphy v. State


Case Number: PCD-2001-1197


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2002 OK CR 32; 54 P.3d 556; 2002 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 37; 73 O.B.A.J. 2491



September 4, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Post-conviction relief denied at Murphy v. State, 2003 OK CR 6, 66 P.3d 456, 2003 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 7 (Okla. Crim. App., Mar. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murphy v. State, 2002 OK CR 24, 47 P.3d 876, 2002 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 27 (Okla. Crim. App., May 22, 2002)



DISPOSITION:  Petitioner's Application for Post-Conviction Relief, Motion for Evidentiary Hearing, and Motion to Hold Post-Conviction Case in Abeyance are denied as to all issues except proposition three; petitioner's Application for Post-Conviction Relief and Motion for Evidentiary Hearing are granted with respect to the issue of mental retardation and the matter is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder in the District Court of McIntosh County, Oklahoma, and sentenced to death. Following affirmance of his conviction and sentence on direct appeal, defendant filed an application for postconviction relief asserting in part an Atkins claim of mental retardation, together with a motion for evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his trial and appellate counsel failed to adequately investigate, develop, and present available mitigating evidence. The court found that, although defendant's post-conviction affidavits established more "mitigating" evidence than was developed at trial, they did not provide a reasonable probability the sentencing result would have been different if competent counsel had presented the materials and explained their significance. Defendant asserted that his jury trial rights were violated by the district court's failure to instruct the jury that it must find the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt. The court disagreed, holding that Apprendi did not invalidate the State's capital sentencing scheme. Defendant also asserted that, due to his mild mental retardation, his execution would violate the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment and offend contemporary standards of decency. The court found that defendant's mental retardation claims had merit in view of the substantive Eighth Amendment limitation imposed under Atkins on the state's power to take the life of a mentally retarded offender.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the district court for an evidentiary hearing on the sole issue of defendant's Atkins claim of mental retardation.

Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by, Judgment entered by Lockett v. Workman, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 157157 (W.D. Okla., Jan. 19, 2011)
Transferred by, in part Lockett v. Evans, 2014 OK 28, 2014 Okla. LEXIS 35 (Okla., 2014)

DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of Noble County (Oklahoma) of conspiracy, first degree burglary, assault with a dangerous weapon, forcible oral sodomy, first degree rape, kidnapping, robbery by force or fear, and first degree murder. Defendant was sentenced to death, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and others beat the victims and the others sexually assaulted two females. One of the victims was murdered. Defendant was charged and convicted of various crimes, including first degree murder. The court upheld the convictions and sentence on appeal. Defendant's constitutional rights were not violated even though the trial court conducted portions of the voir dire outside the presence of defendant. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and death sentence.

Clark v. Hall


Case Number: HB-2002-889


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2002 OK CR 29; 53 P.3d 416; 2002 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 34



July 24, 2002, Decided



DISPOSITION: Writ of habeas corpus granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was arrested for the misdemeanor offense of engaging/offering to engage in an act of prostitution. The District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) set her bail at the nondiscretionary amount of $ 15,000 pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1101.1 (supp. 2002). Petitioner's request for a reduction of bail was denied by respondent special trial court judge. Petitioner then filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner alleged that Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1101.1 (supp. 2002), was unconstitutional because it deprived those in custody of the opportunity for an individualized determination to bail, violated the constitutional doctrine of separation of powers, and was being used as punishment and not merely to ensure the presence of an accused at future proceedings. The special judge averred the legislature recognized that in crimes involving prostitution, minimum bail amounts and/or personal recognizance bonds did not serve to protect the interests of society or the neighborhoods plagued by this unlawful activity. The judge concluded Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1101.1 (supp. 2002), was the legislature's attempt to reduce the futility and hopelessness felt by citizens outraged such conduct was continuing in their neighborhoods. The appellate court found that the statute was unconstitutional because it violated the due process rights of Oklahoma citizens to an individualized determination to bail guaranteed by Okla. Const. art. II, § 7. The appellate court noted that the amount of an appearance bond should never be set at a high amount solely for the purpose of punishing an accused.


OUTCOME: Petitioner demonstrated that her confinement was unlawful. The matter was remanded to the trial court for a proper bail determination.

Alexander v. State


Case Number: F-2000-472


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2002 OK CR 23; 48 P.3d 110; 2002 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 28; 73 O.B.A.J. 1667



May 30, 2002, Decided



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In separate cases, defendant pled guilty to a misdemeanor and two charges of possession of methamphetamine and was sentenced to 20 years or completion of drug court in the latter two cases . The State filed an application to terminate defendant from drug court for violations of the terms of his drug court agreement. The District Court of Hughes County (Oklahoma) terminated defendant from drug court and imposed sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged numerous errors, including a denial of due process because the district court was part of his drug court team. The appellate court conducted a review of the drug court program under the Oklahoma Drug Court Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, §§ 471 to -471.11 et seq. (Supp. 1998). The appellate court held there was more than sufficient independent, corroborative evidence presented at the termination hearing to find defendant had violated the terms of his drug court contract. Defendant claimed that the proceedings were inherently biased because they were conducted by the district judge, a member of the drug court team. The appellate court held defendant's allegations of bias did not constitute error sufficient to require reversal. There was no indication that defendant was deprived of a fair proceeding. Moreover, defendant never requested the judge's recusal which waived the issue. However, the appellate court concluded that in the future, if an application to terminate a drug court participant was filed, and a defendant objected to the drug court team judge hearing the matter by filing a motion to recuse, the defendant's application for recusal should be granted.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order terminating defendant's participation in drug court was affirmed.

Murphy v. State


Case No. D-2000-705


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Murphy v. Oklahoma, 538 U.S. 985, 123 S. Ct. 1795, 155 L. Ed. 2d 678, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 3059 (Apr. 21, 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Request denied by, Stay denied by, Motion denied by Murphy v. Sirmons, 497 F. Supp. 2d 1257, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 56161 (E.D. Okla., Aug. 1, 2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Request denied by, Remanded by, in part In re Murphy, 2012 U.S. App. LEXIS 27395 (10th Cir., Nov. 1, 2012)

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the McIntosh County District Court (Oklahoma) of first degree murder. He was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13 (C) (1991), the mandatory death sentence review, the supreme court found that the death sentence was supported by the evidence. The jury found the existence of two aggravating circumstance, the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel, and that there was a probability that defendant would commit criminal acts of violence that constituted a continuing threat to society. There was evidence defendant discussed killing the victim before the crime, the crime was particularly brutal, and there was evidence defendant intended to kill the victim's relatives, and took steps in that regard. Defendant presented mitigating evidence that he had no significant prior criminal history, his capacity to appreciate the criminality of his conduct was impaired by alcohol, that he was under the influence of an emotional disturbance by virtue of his alcohol dependence, and he cooperated with authorities. After carefully weighing the aggravating circumstance and the mitigating evidence, along with the errors alleged in the appeal, the supreme court found that the sentence of death was factually substantiated and appropriate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Howerton


Case Number: SR-2001-242


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2002 OK CR 17; 46 P.3d 154; 2002 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 18; 73 O.B.A.J. 1257



April 11, 2002, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] DECLARATION OF UNCONSTITUTIONALITY OF STATUTE REVERSED AND MATTER REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with one count of owning or operating a chop shop and five counts of knowingly concealing stolen property. The District Court of Delaware County (Oklahoma) ruled that Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 4209.8 (Supp. 1998) was unconstitutional, suppressed the evidence discovered during an inspection, as well as evidence recovered pursuant to a follow-up search warrant, and granted defendant's motion to quash. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Officers went to defendant's business to conduct an administrative inspection. The visit was prompted by discrepancies on some title applications that defendant submitted to the tax commission. Defendant informed officers that he was buying boat motors from out of state and that the paperwork he was getting with the motors was off one or two numbers, so he was changing the paperwork to match the serial numbers on the motors and then sending the paperwork in with the title applications. The officers went to another building where there were about 200 outboard motors and two or three boats. A check of a serial number indicated one of the boats was stolen. At this point the administrative inspection was ceased, and a search warrant was obtained. The court ruled as follows: (1) as defendant's business was searched at a reasonable time, during business hours, he did not have standing to argue that the statute should be held facially void because other persons could conceivably be searched at an unreasonable time; and (2) the statute was limited to business hours and complied with the 4th Amendment's prohibition of unreasonable searches and seizures.


OUTCOME: Declaration of the statute as unconstitutional was reversed.

 

299 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Burleson v. Saffle


Case Number: CQ-2002-140


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2002 OK CR 15; 46 P.3d 150; 2002 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 14; 73 O.B.A.J. 1141



March 27, 2002, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Court of Appeals for the Tenth Circuit submitted a question for certification, requesting clarification on the interpretation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 652(B) (Supp. 1992), prohibiting the use of a vehicle to facilitate the discharge of a firearm (drive-by shootings).


OVERVIEW: The court previously held that, where a vehicle was used to facilitate the intentional discharge of a weapon during a single transaction or shooting event, only one count of using a vehicle to facilitate the intentional discharge of a firearm was appropriate. The certified question asked whether the statute had the same meaning under Oklahoma law on May 2, 1997, the day defendant's criminal conviction for two counts of violating the statute was affirmed? The question turned on the intent of the legislature, whether the statute criminalized a course of action, rather than a discrete act. The court determined that the statute's meaning was the same as it was on May 2, 1997. The court ruled that the legislature intended to impose an additional punishment on persons who committed drive-by shootings by allowing more than one prosecution when there were multiple victims. Furthermore, the court ruled that its prior case was wrongly decided and must be overruled.


OUTCOME: Certified question answered.

 

300 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Banks v. State


Case No. D-1999-1483


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2002 OK CR 9; 43 P.3d 390; 2002 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 6; 73 O.B.A.J. 681



February 21, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied: Banks v. Oklahoma, 154 L. Ed. 2d 811, 123 S. Ct. 898, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 152 (U.S. 2003).
Writ of certiorari denied Banks v. Oklahoma, 537 U.S. 1126, 123 S. Ct. 898, 154 L. Ed. 2d 811, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 152 (2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Banks v. Workman, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 92262 (N.D. Okla., Sept. 3, 2010)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) convicted defendant of first degree murder, and he was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court determined that viewing the evidence in a light most favorable to the State, the victim was taken forcibly from her parking lot, and transported to an apartment, where she was forced to have intercourse. Upon completion of these crimes, the victim was executed on the roadside. All the elements of felony murder in the commission of rape or kidnapping were satisfied. The only question for the jury was who committed the crimes. Defendant was one of the rapists, and he may or may not have actually pulled the trigger; if he did not, he may nevertheless have encouraged it. The court ruled that a rational jury could have convicted defendant of malice aforethought murder. Furthermore, any error in allowing a witness to be questioned after he attempted to invoke his Fifth Amendment privilege was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, because it did not contribute to the jury's verdict. The evidence established that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances and that the jury was not influenced by passion, prejudice or any arbitrary factors.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Frederick v. State

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, sentencing him to death upon his conviction of murder in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was tried by jury, convicted of murder in the first degree, and sentenced to death. That conviction was reversed and remanded for a new trial. Upon retrial before a jury, appellant was again found guilty of murder in the first degree, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (1989), and punishment was again set at death. The appellate court granted review, and concluded that appellant did in fact receive a fair trial. The death penalty was warranted because two statutory aggravating circumstances were found to exist beyond a reasonable doubt. First, the murder was committed for the purpose of avoiding or preventing a lawful arrest or prosecution. Second, there existed a probability that the defendant would commit criminal acts of violence that would constitute a continuing threat to society.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

302 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thomason


No. SR-2000-859


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2001 OK CR 27; 33 P.3d 930; 2001 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 29; 72 O.B.A.J. 2954



October 3, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 5, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMANCHE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE LEO A. WATSON, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in a three count multi-county grand jury indictment. The indictment was dismissed and refiled as an information in the District Court of Comanche County, Oklahoma, charging defendant with caretaker neglect (count one), obstructing an officer (count two), and attempted subornation of perjury (count three). Appellee's motions to dismiss count one and to quash, set aside, and dismiss count two were granted. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the director of a nursing home. The caretaker neglect charge arose from the care or lack thereof that a 91-year-old resident of the home received prior to his death. The charge of obstructing an officer arose from circumstances where an investigator from the Medicaid Fraud Control Unit of the Attorney General's Office was refused access to photographs of a resident, as well as the resident's medical records and the depicted resident. The State was unsuccessful in convicting defendant. On appeal, the State alleged that the district court erred in ruling that Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 843.1 (1991) was unconstitutional. The court of criminal appeals held that § 843.1 was not unconstitutional since it was not so vague as to be violative of due process; it was never repealed; and it gave defendant adequate notice. Also, it was not unconstitutional because caretaker was defined differently in rules and regulations governing nursing homes, and because it lent itself to selective prosecution. Further, the Medicaid Fraud Control Unit was entitled to a non-Medicaid patient's confidential records under the circumstances of this case.


OUTCOME: The orders were reversed and remanded.

Williams v. State

DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for Post-Conviction Relief DENIED. Motion for Correction of Order Denying Motion to Reconsider Order Denying Motion for Leave of Court to Conduct Pre-Filing Factual Discovery with Subpoena Power for Documents and Testimony DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applied for post conviction relief from an order of the Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma, affirming defendant's conviction of first degree murder and assault and battery with intent to kill.


OVERVIEW: The court found that: (1) defense counsel's failure to raise the claim of error as to the trial court's failure to give instructions in addition to the uniform jury instructions, and counsel's failure to challenge the clemency scheme did not deny defendant the effective assistance of counsel, because counsel's performance was not deficient under prevailing professional norms; (2) the claim of ineffective assistance of counsel for failing to present additional mitigating evidence was raised and addressed on direct appeal, and barred by res judicata; (3) challenges to the imposition of the death penalty by the jury as cruel and unusual punishment consisted of claims that could have previously raised grounds for review, but were not, were deemed waived, and grounds for review which were properly presented had no merit; and (4) defendant failed show by clear and convincing evidence the materials contained in the verified motion for evidentiary hearing on post-conviction claims had or were likely to support in law and fact, to be relevant to adjudication of the allegations raised in the application for post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The application for post-conviction relief was denied; the motion for correction of order denying the motion to reconsider order denying motion for leave of court to conduct pre-filing factual was denied.

 

304 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Cipriano v. State


No. F-2000-890


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2001 OK CR 25; 32 P.3d 869; 2001 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 26; 72 O.B.A.J. 2629



September 4, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 11, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE RAY C. ELLIOTT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) that convicted him of first degree murder and sentenced him to life in prison without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, appellant argued that: (1) the trial court failed to properly instruct the jury; (2) the trial court erred in excluding evidence of the deceased's father's extensive and violent criminal history; (3) the trial court erred in failing to admonish the jury not to consider the matter of parole; and (4) his sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole was excessive and cruel and unusual under the circumstances. Upon review, the appellate court affirmed the judgment. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in rejecting appellant's requested jury instructions. Evidence of the specific nature of the deceased's father's violent history was collateral to the issue of appellant's guilt or innocence and not relevant as it did not have any tendency to make more or less probable the fact that appellant intended to kill the deceased. The trial court's refusal to admonish the jury not to consider matters outside the jury instructions was not prejudicial, as it would have been merely repetitive of the written instructions. Appellant's sentence was properly based in the evidence and supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hoover v. State

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the District Court of Oklahoma County denying his motion for expungement and sealing of record resulting from criminal charges for which he was acquitted.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was tried by jury and acquitted of several counts of lewd molestation. He filed a timely appeal of this order. On review, the case was remanded to the district court for a new hearing on the petition for expungement and sealing of records. The trial court did not afford appellant the presumption of harm. This error required relief.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the district court for a new hearing on the petition for expungement and sealing of records.

Abshier v. State


Case No. F-98-188


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2001 OK CR 13; 28 P.3d 579; 2001 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 12; 72 O.B.A.J. 1819



May 24, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 12, 2001. July 16, 2001 the Appellate Counsel filed a Motion to Reconsider the Court's Order of July 12, 2001 Denying Rehearing.
Order Issued August 6, 2001 Denying Appellants' Motion to File Supplemental Brief and Motion to Reconsider Denial of Petition for Rehearing. Certiorari Denied April 15, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 2429.
Writ of certiorari denied Abshier v. Oklahoma, 535 U.S. 991, 122 S. Ct. 1548, 152 L. Ed. 2d 472, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 2429 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Abshier v. Workman, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 85061 (W.D. Okla., Aug. 18, 2010)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, convicted appellant of first degree murder of a child in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(C) (1991). The jury found two aggravating circumstances existed: that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel, and that it was probable that appellant would commit future acts of violence. The trial court sentenced appellant to death. Appellant perfected his appeal.


OVERVIEW: The state supreme court held, inter alia: (1) because appellant could not hope to win in the guilt or innocence stage, it was proper trial strategy for counsel to focus on obtaining a life without parole sentence by conceding appellant's guilt, and appellant acquiesced in the strategy; (2) such statements did not waive any of appellant's rights, nor did they relieve the State of its burden; (3) the State presented overwhelming evidence of appellant's guilt; (4) counsel's strategy in voir dire and opening statement resulted in several jurors being excused; (5) counsel was not ineffective; (6) the refusal to excuse one juror for cause was not error; (7) expert opinion testimony that the child was conscious and crying during the beating was properly admitted; (8) evidence of prior acts of violence by appellant against the victim was admissible to rebut his statement that she was the victim of an automobile-pedestrian accident; (9) photographs of the victim were relevant, (10) there was sufficient evidence for a jury to find the aggravating circumstances, proven beyond a reasonable doubt, outweighed mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence of death for first degree murder of a child was affirmed.

Williams v. State

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 17, 2001. Counsel Corrected June 21, 2001. Certiorari Denied January 7, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 19.
Post-conviction relief denied at Williams v. State, 2001 OK CR 24, 31 P.3d 1046, 2001 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 25 (Okla. Crim. App., 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Williams v. Oklahoma, 534 U.S. 1092, 122 S. Ct. 836, 151 L. Ed. 2d 716, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 19 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Williams v. Workman, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 22704 (N.D. Okla., Mar. 7, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE THOMAS C. GILLERT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS and SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which convicted the appellant of first-degree murder, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991), and assault and battery with intent to kill, after former conviction of two felonies, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 652 (1992).Appellant raises twenty (20) propositions of error in his appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the appellant raised 20 propositions of error, including that the trial court erred in excusing a prospective juror for cause because of her views on capital punishment without ascertaining whether or not the prospective juror could follow the law despite her views. The court found no abuse of discretion by the trial court in the manner in which it conducted voir dire. The trial court's questions to the prospective juror sufficiently established that she could neither consider nor impose the death penalty in the appellant's case, where the evidence and law warranted its imposition. The trial court's questions were adequate to determine whether the prospective juror could sit as a fair and impartial juror in the case. Appellant also made several allegations that he was denied effective assistance of counsel. The court found that trial counsel made certain omissions and errors, but that these errors were not outside the wide range of professionally competent assistance. The court held that the appellant failed to rebut the presumption that counsel's conduct was professionally reasonable and failed to show that he was denied a fundamentally fair trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Black v. State


No. D-1999-249


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2001 OK CR 5; 21 P.3d 1047; 2001 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 5; 72 O.B.A.J. 858



March 12, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 9, 2001. Certiorari Denied October 29, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 10142.
Writ of certiorari denied Black v. Oklahoma, 534 U.S. 1004, 122 S. Ct. 483, 151 L. Ed. 2d 396, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 10142 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Black v. Workman, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 11809 (W.D. Okla., Feb. 10, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF STEPHENS COUNTY. THE HONORABLE GEORGE W. LINDLEY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Stephens County, Oklahoma, convicting him of murder in the first degree and assault and battery with a deadly weapon and sentencing him to death after finding four aggravating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder in the first degree and assault and battery with a deadly weapon. Defendant was sentenced to death on the murder conviction and 15 years imprisonment for assault and battery with a deadly weapon. On appeal, defendant claimed he was denied his right to select a fair and impartial jury due to the trial court's restrictive voir dire process. The court found that there was no evidence to support defendant's contention that he was not provided with the jury questionnaires. With regard to the sufficiency of the evidence, the court found that the direct and circumstantial evidence presented at trial was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to conclude defendant intended to kill victim when he stabbed him 11 times, his statements notwithstanding.


OUTCOME: Judgment and sentence affirmed; the court found no error that warranted relief. Any irregularities or errors were harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.

Pickens v. State

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2001 OK CR 3; 19 P.3d 866; 2001 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2; 72 O.B.A.J. 388



January 24, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 16, 2001. Writ of certiorari denied: Pickens v. Oklahoma, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4981 (U.S. June 28, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied Pickens v. Oklahoma, 536 U.S. 961, 122 S. Ct. 2668, 153 L. Ed. 2d 842, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4981 (2002)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Pickens v. State, 2003 OK CR 16, 74 P.3d 601, 2003 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 16 (Okla. Crim. App., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Pickens v. State, 1994 OK CR 74, 885 P.2d 678, 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 84 (Okla. Crim. App., 1994)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] AFFIRMED; REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR A NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted in the Creek County (Oklahoma) District Court of first degree murder while in the commission of robbery with a dangerous weapon, Okla. Stat. tit. 221, § 701.7 (Supp. 1989), and feloniously carrying a firearm, Okla. Stat. tit. 221, § 1283 (Supp. 1989), and sentenced to death. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree murder while committing robbery with a dangerous weapon, and feloniously carrying a firearm. The jury found three aggravating circumstances and set punishment at death on the murder conviction. The court of appeals affirmed in part, holding that (1) an officer's search warrant affidavit did not include misleading ballistics information, and the magistrate was presented with other facts sufficient to establish probable cause; (2) appellant's decision to waive counsel and his subsequent confession were valid, even thought his court-appointed attorney on other charges was not informed of his arrest; (3) other crimes evidence was properly admitted; (4) there was no need to instruct the jury on a lesser offense that did not include use of a weapon; and (5) appellant knowingly waived his right to present mitigating evidence by family members at the sentencing hearing. The court reversed on one issue, finding that one jury instruction misled the jury to believe appellant may have had prior firearms convictions. Therefore the firearm conviction was reversed and remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: Murder conviction and sentence affirmed; the search warrant was supported by probable cause, appellant validly waived counsel before questioning, other crimes evidence was admissible, the jury received proper instructions, and appellant knowingly waived his right to present certain mitigating evidence at sentencing. The firearm conviction was reversed and remanded for a new trial, due to a misleading jury instruction.

Hooks v. State

Modified by Hooks v. State, 2001 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 6 (Okla. Crim. App., 2001)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hooks v. State, 2001 OK CR 7, 22 P.3d 231, 2001 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 7 (Okla. Crim. App., 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Hooks v. Oklahoma, 534 U.S. 963, 122 S. Ct. 371, 151 L. Ed. 2d 282, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 9653 (2001)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by Hooks v. Workman, 606 F.3d 715, 2010 U.S. App. LEXIS 10564 (10th Cir. Okla., May 25, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DANIEL L. OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, convicted defendant of five counts of murder in the first degree in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991). The jury then sentenced defendant to death on each count. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised several issues of error. The appellate court denied relief, holding, inter alia, defendant did not show: (1) he was denied a jury composed of a fair cross-section of the community caused by systematic exclusion of African-Americans; (2) his story raised a credible, reasonable hypothesis of innocence as the case was built on strong circumstantial evidence; (3) a discovery violation, or the admission of other crimes and hearsay evidence, resulted in a miscarriage of justice or substantially violated his statutory or constitutional rights; (4) the Allen instruction given was improper, or that the jury misunderstood the law; (5) trial counsel was ineffective; or (6) the admission of victim impact evidence was erroneous. Although the prosecution presented misleading evidence in the first stage of trial and engaged in egregiously improper argument in both stages, the jury was not misled. Thus, the prosecutorial misconduct did not affect defendant's rights. Finally, the combination of errors did not infect the trial or sentencing proceeding with unfairness, and the death sentence was factually substantiated and appropriate.


OUTCOME: Finding no error warranting modification, the court affirmed the judgment and death sentence.

Myers v. State


No. D 1998-646


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2000 OK CR 25; 17 P.3d 1021; 2000 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 24; 71 O.B.A.J. 3246



December 8, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 29, 2001. Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 6719.
Writ of certiorari denied Myers v. Oklahoma, 534 U.S. 900, 122 S. Ct. 228, 151 L. Ed. 2d 163, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 6719 (2001)
Post-conviction relief denied at Myers v. State, 2005 OK CR 22, 2005 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 18 (Okla. Crim. App., 2005)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged is conviction and death sentence, in the the District Court of Rogers County (Oklahoma), for murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found by the jury to have had sexual intercourse with and then to have killed the female victim. Appellant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. Evidence against appellant included a DNA match between appellant and sperm found in victim, a prior crime of a sexual assault upon and threat to kill a female, that victim was an acquaintance of appellant, and a fellow prisoner's testimony that appellant had admitted killing the victim. The trial court conducted an in camera reliability hearing prior to admission of the fellow prisoner's testimony. The court referred to the greater latitude for admissibility of like occurrences evidence in sexual assault cases. The admitted photographs were relevant and not unduly gruesome. The aggravating factors found, and reweighed against mitigating factors by the court, included that the murder was heinous, atrocious, or cruel, appellant had committed a prior felony, appellant was a continuing threat to society, and the murder was committed to avoid arrest. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and death sentence.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed. Whether to disqualify a juror for cause rested within trial court's sound discretion. Evidence that appellant previously sexually assaulted and threatened to kill a woman was admissible to show appellant's motive and intent to kill the victim in this case. There was proof appellant killed to avoid arrest. Certain victim photographs were properly admitted.

 

312 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Macy v. Bragg


No. PR-2000-1122


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2000 OK CR 21; 13 P.3d 503; 2000 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 21; 71 O.B.A.J. 2931



October 27, 2000, Decided  
October 27, 2000, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought a writ of prohibition and/or writ of mandamus reversing respondent judge's order, that struck a jury panel which had been summoned in a criminal case, on the ground that respondent lacked authority to strike the jury panel based upon its racial make-up.


OVERVIEW: Respondent struck the jury panel in a criminal case involving a black defendant, contending that the fact that there was one black prospective juror in the panel did not fairly represent the defendant's peers and was fundamentally unfair. The State sought the reversal of respondent's order. After determining that a writ of mandamus and/or prohibition was the proper vehicle for the State to use, the court granted the petition and reversed the striking of the jury panel. The court held that respondent erred by striking the jury panel because there was no evidence presented that the current method of jury selection in the county systematically excluded distinctive groups within the community. The record was devoid of any evidence that the jury panel was not drawn from a fair cross section of the community; therefore there was no legal justification for respondent to strike the jury panel.


OUTCOME: Petition granted. Respondent had no legal justification to strike the jury panel because no evidence showed that the current method of jury selection in the county systematically excluded distinctive groups within the community or that the jury panel was not drawn from a fair cross section of the community.

Wackerly v. State


F-98-554


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2000 OK CR 15; 12 P.3d 1; 2000 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 16; 71 O.B.A.J. 2132



August 11, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 10, 2000. Certiorari Denied May 14, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3720.
Writ of certiorari denied Wackerly v. Oklahoma, 532 U.S. 1028, 121 S. Ct. 1976, 149 L. Ed. 2d 768, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3720 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Request denied by Wackerly v. Sirmons, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 23320 (E.D. Okla., Mar. 27, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Motion denied by Wackerly v. State, 2010 OK CR 16, 237 P.3d 795, 2010 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 16 (Okla. Crim. App., 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied In re Wackerly, 2010 U.S. App. LEXIS 27028 (10th Cir. Okla., Sept. 3, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SEQUOYA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JOHN GARRETT PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his first degree murder and first degree robbery convictions and death sentence, after a finding of the aggravating factors that murder was committed for the purpose of avoiding or preventing lawful arrest or prosecution and that there existed a probability that appellant would commit criminal acts of violence that would constitute a continuing threat to society, by the District Court of Sequoya County (Oklahoma).


OVERVIEW: Appellant told his wife that they needed money and he was going to do whatever it took to get it. The couple found the victim, who was killed. Later appellant's then-estranged wife implicated him. Appellant was convicted of murder and robbery and sentenced to death. The court affirmed. A voir dire record omission did not affect review of Witherspoon issues. Jurors who said they could vote for the death penalty did not unequivocally say that was the only option they would consider. Although several items not listed in a search warrant were seized, only one was admitted into evidence at trial. That item had been in plain view after a drawer was opened looking for a warrant-specified wallet. Appellant had not objected to the jury going into the hall unattended after deliberations began. Due to third-party testimony that appellant admitted he had killed the victim, the confidential nature of his prior discussions with his wife was lost and her testimony was corroborated. There was robbery even though the victim had been killed first. Appellant's not disguising himself showed the aggravating factor of killing to avoid arrest. A very short victim impact statement had no plain error.


OUTCOME: Convictions and sentence affirmed. Due to third-party testimony that appellant admitted to the killing, the confidentiality of his prior talk with his now-estranged wife was lost and her testimony was corroborated. There was robbery even though the victim may not have known what was happening and had been killed first. Appellant's lack of disguise showed the killing had been to avoid arrest. Gloves in a drawer had been in "plain view."

 

314 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Gilson v. State


No. F-98-606


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2000 OK CR 14; 8 P.3d 883; 2000 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 15; 71 O.B.A.J. 2063



July 26, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 29, 2000. Certiorari Denied April 2, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 2796.
Writ of certiorari denied Gilson v. Oklahoma, 532 U.S. 962, 121 S. Ct. 1496, 149 L. Ed. 2d 381, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 2796 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Gilson v. Sirmons, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 55913 (W.D. Okla., Aug. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CLEVELAND COUNTY. THE HONORABLE WILLIAM C. HETHERINGTON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS and SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, criminal, challenged the judgment of the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma) convicting him of first-degree murder, conspiracy to unlawfully remove a dead body, and unlawful removal of a dead body, as charged by appellee, state. During the second trial stage, the jury found the existence of two aggravating circumstances, and recommended the death penalty. The trial court sentenced accordingly.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, criminal, challenged first-degree murder, conspiracy to unlawfully remove a dead body, and unlawful removal of a dead body convictions, as charged by appellee, state. Findings of two aggravating factors resulted in a death sentence. Appellant raised 14 errors, including: unanimous verdict right violation, improper joinder of child abuse and murder counts, denial of fair trial by suggestive child witness interviews, improper defense witness exclusion based on attorney-client privilege waiver, evidence insufficiency for murder and child abuse, vagueness of first-degree murder by child abuse and child abuse statutes, the jury instruction violated ex post facto laws, appellee's statutory definition lowered the proof burden, failure to instruct on lesser included offenses, defective jury instructions based on failure to explain appellee's proof burden, the sentence violated federal and state constitutions, improper court analysis for a death sentence, which was disproportionate, evidence insufficiency and unconstitutionality of the two aggravating factors, ineffective counsel assistance, and error accumulation. The court found no error existed, thereby affirming.


OUTCOME: Judgment and death penalty sentence affirmed since the state criminal appellate court found that no error existed after review of appellant's 14 error assignments.

Bland v. State


No. F-98-152


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2000 OK CR 11; 4 P.3d 702; 2000 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 11; 71 O.B.A.J. 1304



May 16, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 21, 2000.
Certiorari Denied January 8, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 553.
Writ of certiorari denied Bland v. Oklahoma, 531 U.S. 1099, 121 S. Ct. 832, 148 L. Ed. 2d 714, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 553 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Bland v. Sirmons, 459 F.3d 999, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 19819 (10th Cir. Okla., 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at Bland v. State, 2007 OK CR 25, 164 P.3d 1076, 2007 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 24 (Okla. Crim. App., 2007)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT and SENTENCE AFFIRMED and APPLICATION FOR EVIDENTIARY HEARING ON SIXTH AMENDMENT CLAIMS IS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convicted felon appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Tillman County (Oklahoma), convicting him of first degree malice aforethought murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991) with the jury finding the existence of two aggravating circumstances, resulting in the imposition of the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Appellant handyman worked with a fellow handyman on a particular job. After being paid, and spending his entire half of the money received, appellant fatally shot his co-worker. Appellant was later apprehended for driving under the influence, whereupon it was found that he had a sum of cash in his pocket, purportedly that of the victim. Appellant was convicted of first degree malice aforethought murder under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991), and sentenced to death, the jury having found two aggravating circumstances. Appellant challenged both the conviction and the sentence. Judgment was affirmed. A rational trier of fact could have found the existence of the essential elements of first degree malice aforethought murder beyond a reasonable doubt after reviewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the State. Appellant failed to show that but for any unprofessional errors by counsel, the trial result would have been any different. There was no error in the admission of the prior first degree manslaughter conviction to support the prior violent felony aggravator, together with details of a kidnapping to support the continuing threat aggravator.


OUTCOME: Judgment and sentence were affirmed. Application for evidentiary hearing on Sixth Amendment claims was denied. Court found after reviewing evidence in light most favorable to State that rational trier of fact could have found existence of essential elements of first degree malice aforethought murder beyond reasonable doubt. Defense counsel's performance did not undermine proper functioning of adversarial process to effect different trial result.

Selsor v. State


Case No. F-98-531


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2000 OK CR 9; 2 P.3d 344; 2000 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 8



April 10, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 10, 2000. Certiorari Denied May 21, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3875.
Writ of certiorari denied Selsor v. Oklahoma, 532 U.S. 1039, 121 S. Ct. 2002, 149 L. Ed. 2d 1004, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3875 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Selsor v. Workman, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 93348 (N.D. Okla., Sept. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE E.R. (NED) TURNBULL.
Selsor v. Turnbull, 1997 OK CR 61, 947 P.2d 579, 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 61 (Okla. Crim. App., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, tried by jury in Tulsa County District Court (Oklahoma), was convicted of first degree murder, shooting with intent to kill, and robbery with firearms. He was sentenced to death, life imprisonment, and 20 years in accordance with the jury's recommendation. He appealed, asserting errors at trial and constitutional violations.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, shooting with intent to kill, and robbery with firearms. Defendant's trial and sentencing were not made unfair by the denial of individual voir dire and the possibility prospective jurors had lied to be excused. Defendant's ex post facto and equal protection challenges to the death penalty statute had been rejected previously. Separating elements of murder between instructions was not prejudicial. The record showed defendant committed murder during robbery. Pre-trial information was sufficient. Defendant's robbery conviction should have been dismissed as a lesser-included offense. Ex post facto prohibitions were violated when defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment for shooting to kill, since the maximum imprisonment at the time had been 20 years. Inadmissible parts of surviving victim's testimony did not deny defendant a substantial right. Testimony from murdered victim's family fairly encompassed the murder's effects. Defense counsel was not ineffective; any deficiencies were not prejudicial.


OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence for first-degree murder were affirmed. Conviction for robbery with a firearm reversed with instructions to dismiss as an offense whose elements were included in first-degree murder. Conviction for shooting with intent to kill affirmed, but sentence reduced to maximum possible at the time of the offense.

Hammon v. State


Case No. F-97-910


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2000 OK CR 7; 999 P.2d 1082; 2000 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 7



March 28, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 5, 2000. Released for Publication June 5, 2000.
Certiorari Denied January 8, 2001, Reported at; 2001 U.S. LEXIS 418.
Writ of certiorari denied Hammon v. Oklahoma, 531 U.S. 1090, 148 L. Ed. 2d 697, 121 S. Ct. 812, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 418 (2001)
Subsequent appeal at Hammon v. State, 2004 OK CR 13, 2004 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 16 (Okla. Crim. App., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKMULGEE COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE CHARLES S. WOODSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Hammon v. State, 1995 OK CR 33, 898 P.2d 1287, 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 38 (Okla. Crim. App., 1995)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the determination of death sentence by the District Court of Okmulgee County (Oklahoma) following his conviction of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant actively participated in store robberies using a gun. The other participant shot and killed a clerk and wounded two other persons. Defendant was convicted of first degree murder. The jury set punishment at death after finding the requisite four aggravating circumstances. On appeal the court found no error in evaluating evidentiary decisions. Defendant had adequate counsel. Defendant did not carry burden to establish incompetency. Jurors were properly excused. Prosecutor's cross-examination and closing comments were permissible. Intoxication defense applied to specific intent crimes, not felony-murder general intent crime; and mental retardation was not a defense to death sentence. Defendant was not entitled to instructions including threshold requirements defining the least culpable mental state for the death penalty, because U.S. Const. amend. VIII did not require jury to make those findings. The record supported the requisite findings and were made in an adequate proceeding before an appropriate tribunal.


OUTCOME: Death sentence was affirmed because court found no procedural or evidentiary errors, incompetency not proven, intoxication not a defense for general intent felony murder crime, record supported court determination of least culpable state threshold for death penalty, and aggravating circumstances requirements and mental retardation not a defense to death sentence.

 

318 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


No. F-96-1102


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2000 OK CR 6; 998 P.2d 1225; 2000 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 6; 71 O.B.A.J. 578



February 25, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 30, 2000. Certiorari Denied February 20, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 1302.
Writ of certiorari denied Taylor v. Oklahoma, 531 U.S. 1157, 121 S. Ct. 1109, 148 L. Ed. 2d 978, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 1302 (2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: Taylor v. State, 1998 OK CR 64, 972 P.2d 864, 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 61 (Okla. Crim. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant filed an appeal from a judgment of the Pittsburg County District Court (Oklahoma), in which a jury found him guilty of murder in the first degree and three counts of shooting with intent to kill and recommended the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of murder and sentenced to death, appealed, challenging jury selection, jury instructions, claiming insufficient evidence, and ineffective counsel. The court affirmed. The record did not support appellant's claim that jury selection violated the Equal Protection Clause. Since appellant gave a detailed account of the events and his conduct, he failed to show he was sufficiently intoxicated to raise a reasonable doubt of his ability to form specific intent, thus he was not entitled to a manslaughter instruction. The evidence showing appellant killed one person and shot three others was sufficient to support the aggravating finding that appellant knowingly created a great risk of death to more than one person. Finally, defense counsel's strategy to eliminate malice aforethought by arguing appellant was on drugs, did not know the deceased, and shot him as a reflex, was a sound and valid trial strategy.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Imposition of the death penalty was proper because evidence that appellant killed one person and shot three others supported the aggravating finding that he knowingly created a great risk of death to more than one person, and the murder was committed to avoid or prevent a lawful arrest.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed mandatory appellate review from jury-imposed death penalty for first degree murder, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991) and shooting with intent to kill, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 652 (1991), from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), alleging numerous constitutional and trial procedural errors.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of first degree murder, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991) and shooting with intent to kill, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 652 (1991). The jury found the existence of one aggravating circumstance, that appellant knowingly created a great risk of death to more than one person, and recommended death. The trial court sentenced appellant to death. The appellate court affirmed, rejecting appellant's several points of error including denial of appellant's due process constitutional rights under U.S. Const. amends. V, VI, VIII, XIV and Okla. Const. art. II, §§ 7, 9, 19, 20, challenges to the prosecutor's use of peremptory challenges, prosecutorial misconduct, ineffective counsel, and admissibility of confession and other evidence. The appellate court further held that under the mandatory review of death sentences under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13(C)(1991), the sentence was factually substantiated and not imposed under any arbitrary factor.


OUTCOME: Convictions and death sentence affirmed because, having reviewed all assignments of error raised, including use of peremptory challenges, admission of evidence and prosecutorial misconduct, the appellate court held that the sentence of death to be factually substantiated and not imposed under the influence of passion or any other arbitrary factor.

Stripling v. State ex rel. Okla. Health Care Auth.


Case Number: 114164


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION FOUR


2017 OK CIV APP 6; 394 P.3d 293; 2016 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 59



December 22, 2016, Decided 
January 24, 2017, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals January 24, 2017.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE PATRICIA G. PARRISH, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The district court properly denied the Oklahoma Health Care Authority's motion to dismiss a doctor's appeal on jurisdictional grounds because she filed her second case and paid the required filing fees within the 30-day period specified by Okla. Stat. art. 12, § 951(b) (2011) and the second petition was properly treated as a transfer of her first case; [2]-The district court erred in granting the Authority's motion to dismiss the doctor's appeal for failure to state a claim because the motion was not predicated on one of the grounds authorized by Okla. Sup. Ct. R. 1.6, Okla. Stat. tit. 12, ch. 15, app 1 (Supp. 2013)--the alleged denial of due process-- transformed the appeal into a "summary process" not authorized by Okla. Stat. art. 12, § 951 (2011), and permitted use of district court motion practice to supplement the record in the district court, which was prohibited.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed in part, reversed in part, and matter remanded.

Davis v. Okla. Dep't of Corr.


Case Number: 113773


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION FOUR


2016 OK CIV APP 23; 370 P.3d 1231; 2016 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 3



March 14, 2016, Decided 
April 14, 2016, Mandate Issued

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE ROGER H. STUART, TRIAL JUDGE.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The district court properly dismissed, for failure to state a claim on which relief could be granted, defendant's petition for declaratory and injunctive relief regarding the Oklahoma Sex Offenders Registration Act, Okla. Atrium Trs II, L.P. v. Univ. of Cent. Okla.


Case Number: 111301


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION I


2014 OK CIV APP 84; 336 P.3d 478; 2014 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 60



September 18, 2014, Decided 
October 15, 2014, Mandate Issued

Const. art. 13-B was not a debt of the State under Okla. Const. art. 10, § 23 or Okla. Stat. tit. 62, §§ 34.41 or 34.49 of the State Finance Act, inasmuch as the Legislature could not be forced to appropriate funds to pay the university's agreed-to obligation.


OUTCOME: Order reversed and case remanded.

State ex rel. Edmondson v. Grand River Enters. Six Nations, Ltd.

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Grand River Enters. v. Oklahoma, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 8670 (U.S., Dec. 2, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-When finding, under Okla. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

DISPOSITION: SUSTAINED.

Under the competent evidence standard of review, respondent employee's testimony and her physician's report supported the determination she suffered injury.


OUTCOME: Judgment sustained.

Harvey v. Auto Plus of Woodward


Case Number: 109803; Consol. w/109805


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2012 OK CIV APP 92; 287 P.3d 410; 2012 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 79



September 13, 2012, Decided 
September 13, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: October 11, 2012, Mandate Issued


DISPOSITION:  [***1] SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Employee who suffered cumulative trauma injuries to his hands, arms, shoulders, and spine from pounding windows with his hands and using vibrating tools to install auto glass was not subject to the defense of Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 11(B)(5), because his doctor testified that his subsequent work did not aggravate the injury, and the employee testified that he worked much less due to his owning his own business and help from his son. The court held that based on its express language, the newly enacted standard of review established in Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 340(D) (2011), applied to the employee's appeal, which was filed after the new statute went into effect, although the injuries occurred and the matter was tried prior to the effective date of the statute. Such a statutorily prescribed standard of review did not violate the separation of powers doctrine of Okla. Const. art. IV, ¶ 1.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the landowner was affirmed. The order awarding attorney fees and costs to the landowner was reversed and the case was remanded for a determination of a reasonable attorney fee award and an award of eligible costs.

347 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Dilbeck v. Dilbeck


Case Number: 106885


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2010 OK CIV APP 142; 245 P.3d 630; 2010 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 123



November 8, 2010, Decided 
December 10, 2010, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 10, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF PAWNEE COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE MATTHEW D. HENRY, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the order of the District Court of Pawnee County, Oklahoma, modifying joint child custody and awarding custody of the couple's minor child to appellee father.


OVERVIEW: The parties were divorced in June 2005, and had one child. The parties continued to live together off and on after the decree was entered, and after reconciliation failed in September 2007, apparently continued to work with the parenting coordinator after the coordinator's appointment expired. The parenting coordinator was reappointed, and in July 2008, filed a report recommending that the father be given legal custody of the child. The father's motion to adopt the parenting coordinator's July 2008 report was granted, and the father's motion to modify the decree was granted. The district court awarded sole custody of the child to the father and on its own motion, discharged the parenting coordinator. The appellate court ruled that the district court had jurisdiction to reappoint the parenting coordinator in the case. However, the Parenting Coordinator Act did not authorize the parenting coordinator to change the custody order or make recommendations regarding to whom custody of a minor child should be awarded. The appellate court found that the father failed to meet his burden of proof showing that a change in custody was warranted.


OUTCOME: The district court's order entered on March 20, 2008, reappointing the parenting coordinator and authorizing the parenting coordinator to make recommendations was vacated, and the February 17, 2009 order modifying child custody was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions to deny the father's October 14, 2008 motion to adopt the recommendations in the parenting coordinator's July 2008 report and to modify the decree.

Gentry v. Cotton Elec. Coop., Inc.

349 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Burnett v. Middleton


Case Number: 107772


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2011 OK CIV APP 11; 246 P.3d 464; 2010 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 140



October 8, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals January 28, 2011. Mandate Issued: January 28, 2011
Rehearing denied by Burnett v. Middleton, 2011 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 11 (Okla. Ct. App., Jan. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF PAYNE COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE DONALD L. WORTHINGTON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner filed an action against defendants, various employees of a correctional facility, claiming that defendants violated a variety of his rights in connection with grievance proceedings relating to the prisoner's alleged disciplinary misconduct. The District Court of Payne County, Oklahoma, denied the prisoner's motion for summary judgment and granted defendants' motion to dismiss. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Okla. Stat. tit. 57, § 566.4(K) (Supp. 2006) set forth a procedure for correction officials to review the subject matter of a prisoner's claims in order to provide the court with additional information for the processing of the claim. The prisoner contended that § 566.4(K) was a special law prohibited by Okla. Const. art. 5, § 46, because it affected only inmates rather than all Oklahoma citizens who filed tort claims. On appeal, the court deemed § 566.4's classification of persons sharing the same circumstances to be reasonable and justified. The special report provision of § 566.4(K) was not unconstitutional. The court next found that the trial court correctly dismissed the prisoner's substantive claims. In addition, as an inmate sentenced to life imprisonment, the prisoner did not qualify for earned credits under Okla. Stat. tit. 57, § 138(A) (Supp. 2009) so the disciplinary ruling cost him none, and he had no protected liberty interest in his security classification. The court specifically rejected the prisoner's claims that the trial court wrongfully conducted an evidentiary hearing. The record plainly reflected that no evidentiary hearing was conducted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Mfrs. Guild, Inc. v. City of Enid

August 6, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: September 2, 2010, Mandate Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GARFIELD COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE DENNIS HLADIK, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged a judgment in equity entered by the District Court of Garfield County, Oklahoma, in favor of appellee city and against the owner, allowing demolition of the owner's building and denying the owner's injunctive request to prohibit its destruction and to allow the owner to complete repairs.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the owner had not shown the trial court abused its discretion in finding the property was dilapidated under Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 22-112 (2004) and had become detrimental to the health, safety, or welfare of the general public and the community. The testimony at trial demonstrated by competent evidence significant repair delay and ten dilapidation hearings. The property was in a significant state of decay and partial ruin to the extent that bricks were continuing to fall from time to time, the mortar was brittle and quickly degrading, the patio cover had not been replaced, and the stucco covering was falling off. Section 22-112 was a constitutionally permissible police power statute enacted to protect the general public's health, safety, and welfare. It was rationally related to that goal, satisfied the rational basis test, was clear and unambiguous in its purpose, and thus did not constitute an unconstitutional taking. The police power process exercised by the city and as applied to the owner satisfied constitutional due process. The trial court's findings were not clearly against the weight of the evidence, contrary to law or established principles of equity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Hummer v. State ex rel. Okla. Bd. of Agric.


Case Number: 107261


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2010 OK CIV APP 133; 245 P.3d 1244; 2010 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 113



July 2, 2010, Decided 
November 30, 2010, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 30, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE NOMA D. GURICH, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of an order from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which upheld an order from defendant Oklahoma Board of Agriculture granting a license to defendant applicant for a concentrated swine feeding operation pursuant to the Oklahoma Swine Feeding Operations Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 2, §§ 20-1 to 20-29 (Supp. 2007).


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought a concentrated swine feeding operation license pursuant to the Act. The Board granted the license. The trial court upheld the Board's order. On appeal, the court held that the Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 2, § 20-7(G), did not prohibit the applicant from seeking the license even though the applicant intended to sell the operation after constructing the facility. The administrative proceeding was the determination of the application for the license. The notice given to affected property owners provided plaintiff knowledge of the application and the opportunity to be heard. The Board could not have issued the license to someone other than the applicant based on the application before it. Therefore, the notice gave accurate information as to who would be licensed to own, operate, and manage the proposed facility. Plaintiff's right to due process was not violated by the notice given.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

353 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Wheat v. State ex rel. Tulsa County DA


Case Number: 107728


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION FOUR


2010 OK CIV APP 119; 241 P.3d 1150; 2010 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 96



June 30, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Mandate Issued: October 22, 2010. Released for Publication October 22, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE DAMAN CANTRELL, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed a judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, dismissing her age discrimination lawsuit filed under the Oklahoma Governmental Tort Claims Act against defendant the State.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for a county district attorney's office until she was terminated. The trial court dismissed the employee's age discrimination action, holding that she failed to state a legally cognizable Burk tort claim because she had access to the same remedies as other victims of alleged violations of the State Government Reduction-In-Force and Severance Benefits Act and State employment discrimination. On appeal, the court disagreed and reversed. The court held that the employee was an at-will employee because she did not agree to a contract or otherwise obligate herself to work for a certain period of time, and the district attorney's office did not obligate itself to employ her for a definite duration. The court further held that state employees who alleged age discrimination were part of a larger, single class composed of all victims of employment discrimination, and because the remedies for the different forms of discrimination were disparate, there was a Burk tort remedy for those who alleged employment age discrimination, including the employee.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

354 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Orcutt v. Lloyd Richards Personnel Serv.


Case Number: 107047


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION FOUR


2010 OK CIV APP 77; 239 P.3d 479; 2010 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 58



June 25, 2010, Decided 
June 25, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Mandate Issued: July 23, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING TO REVIEW AN ORDER OF THE WORKERS COMPENSATION COURT. HONORABLE H. THOMAS LEONARD, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant challenged an order of the Oklahoma Workers Compensation Court that denied his claim for compensation for an injury to his left knee that he sustained while playing basketball in an employer's warehouse, arguing that Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 3(13)(d) (2001 and Supp 2005), was unconstitutionally vague in failing to set forth what injuries received during recreational or social activities are to be deemed non-compensable.


OVERVIEW: The claimant worked for respondent, a temporary agency, that assigned him to work for an employer in its warehouse. The warehouse contained a small basketball court that workers were permitted to use after work and on breaks. During a lunch break, the claimant was playing basketball when he injured his knee. He applied for compensation, but his claim was denied based upon a determination that the injury was sustained in the course of a recreational activity and did not arise out of the claimant's employment under Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 3(13)(a) and (d) (2001 and Supp 2005). On review, the court held that, because the challenged order did not address the issue of subsection (d)'s constitutionality, there was no decision on that issue to review. The state legislature's prerogative to exclude from compensability any injury to a worker incurred during work-related recreational and social activities was not an unconstitutional exercise of its power to legislate.


OUTCOME: The order denying compensation benefits was affirmed.

 

355 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Mayberry


Case Number: 107035


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2010 OK CIV APP 94; 241 P.3d 663; 2010 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 76



May 14, 2010, Decided 
October 8, 2010, Mandate Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CREEK COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE DOUGLAS W. GOLDEN, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, who were alleged landowners, sought review of a decision of the District Court of Creek County (Oklahoma), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, the Secretary of the United States Department of the Interior. In the land dispute case regarding a tax deed, the Secretary had filed a motion for summary judgment for the protection of the interests of Indian defendants owning restricted land.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the Secretary's motion for summary judgment on the basis that the tax deed in the underlying action was void because the provisions of § 6(e) of the Act of August 4, 1947, required notice to be served on the Bureau of Indian Affairs prior to the sale of restricted property for delinquent taxes. The landowners argued that the law should not have applied because county treasurers and lawyers were generally ignorant of the statute and because there were no state appellate cases and only one Oklahoma federal district court case construing it. The court upheld the decision because just as everyone was charged with knowledge of the United States Statutes at Large, once a statute had been published, all citizens were on notice of its contents as a matter of law. The landowners also argued that the trial court abused its discretion in its determination that they had not met their burden of proof to establish title by adverse possession. However, neither the payment of taxes nor the recording of a deed constituted possession. Thus, the payment of taxes and the recording of a deed without more did not establish prescriptive title.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

356 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Gonzales v. State


Case Number: 106788


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2010 OK CIV APP 62; 238 P.3d 954; 2010 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 41



March 31, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Mandate Issued: June 11, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE BARBARA SWINTON, TRIAL JUDGE.
Miller v. Gonzales, 2010 OK CIV APP 56, 239 P.3d 163, 2010 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 36 (Okla. Ct. App., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, VACATED, AND REMANDED. WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO DISMISS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State and a city, sought review of a summary judgment entered by the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, in favor of plaintiff dog kennel owner in his declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 22-115.1 (2008). Defendants also sought review of an order denying their motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Section 22-115.1 restricted the location of dog kennels near schools or licensed day care facilities; the owner operated a kennel within 2500 feet of a school and day care facility. The trial court determined the statute was unconstitutional as applied to the owner. The owner lacked standing to challenge the statute's constitutionality because, at the time of its enactment, the owner did not have a license to operate the kennel, even though he had obtained zoning variances, and thus had no vested right to continue operating his kennel without a license. A prior order granting zoning variances did not create a vested right in a kennel license as the owner had not completed all the steps necessary to obtain a license; the owner still had to comply with the building code by providing a handicapped restroom on the premises. Because the owner lacked standing, the court did not reach the issue of whether the statute violated Okla. Const. art. 5, § 52.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, vacated the summary judgment in favor of the owner, and remanded the action with instructions to dismiss.
