Miller v. Gonzales


Case Number: 106771


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2010 OK CIV APP 56; 239 P.3d 163; 2010 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 36



March 8, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Mandate Issued: June 4, 2010.
Related proceeding at Gonzales v. State, 2010 OK CIV APP 62, 238 P.3d 954, 2010 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 41 (Okla. Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CLEVELAND COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE TOM A. LUCAS, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school representative sought injunctive relief to prohibit defendant from operating his kennel in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 22-115.1 (Supp. 2008). Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute. The District Court of Cleveland County, Oklahoma, granted summary judgment for plaintiff representative and intervenor, the State of Oklahoma. Defendant's motion for a new trial was denied. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted he was operating a kennel with 25 dogs in Oklahoma City without a license and within 2500 feet of representative's school. Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 22-115.1 (Supp. 2008) restricted the location of dog kennels in certain locations near schools or day care facilities. Thus, the representative of the school had a right to seek injunctive relief. Defendant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 22-115.1, because he had no vested right that entitled him to constitutional protection for the unlawful operation of his unlicensed kennel. A previous order concerning a zoning ordinance did not create a vested right in defendant to operate his kennel without a license.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

358 of 423 DOCUMENTS


O'Brien Oil, L.L.C. v. Norman


Case No. 107,001


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2010 OK CIV APP 23; 233 P.3d 413; 2010 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 3; 173 Oil & Gas Rep. 492



January 22, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LOGAN COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE DONALD L. WORTHINGTON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, a lessee of minerals, sought a judgment declaring its right to use an abandoned wellbore located on appellant landowners' surface estate. Upon cross-motions for summary judgment, the District Court of Logan County (Oklahoma) granted the lessee's motion for summary judgment and denied the landowners' motion for summary judgment. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the 1980s, a prior lessee abandoned and plugged the wellbore at issue with cement, leaving the casing in place. The landowners acquired the surface estate in 1989. The lessee obtained valid leases of the minerals underlying the landowners' surface estate and obtained a permit to re-enter the plugged well from the Oklahoma Corporation Commission. On appeal, the court concluded that the trial court erred in denying the landowners' motion for summary judgment on their claim to compensation for use of the casing and wellbore. First, the casing of the well clearly became a part of the surface estate upon the prior lessee's failure to remove it within a reasonable time. The landowners also owned the plugged and abandoned wellbore. Second, the landowners did not suffer any unconstitutional taking of their property as a result of the lessee's mineral operations. Third, the landowners' right to compensation for use of the abandoned wellbore should be determined under the Oklahoma Surface Damages Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 52, §§ 318.2 to 318.9 (Supp. 1982), but the landowners' right to compensation for use of the casing should be measured by the rental value of the casing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the trial court's order denying the landowners' motion for summary judgment on the issue of the landowners' claim to compensation for use of the casing and wellbore. The court affirmed the trial court's order in all other respects. The court remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

359 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Arrow Trucking Co. v. Jimenez


Case No. 106, 729


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2010 OK CIV APP 9; 231 P.3d 741; 2009 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 119



December 30, 2009, Decided 
December 30, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals February 1, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING TO REVIEW AN ORDER OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT. HONORABLE GENE PRIGMORE, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, employer and another, sought review of an order of respondent Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Court in which respondent employee was awarded temporary total disability payments (TTD) and permanent partial disability payments (PPD) and denied the employer's request for overpayment of TTD.


OVERVIEW: The employee had soft tissue injuries and no surgery or surgery recommendation. The employer asserted that the trial court erred by awarding the employee 14 weeks and one day of TTD and by denying the employer's request for credit for overpayment of TTD because the employee was only entitled to eight weeks of TTD. The court agreed and vacated the TTD award and the denial of overpayment of TTD because the employee was only entitled to eight weeks of TTD pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 22(3)(d) (Supp. 2007). Because surgery was neither recommended nor performed, § 22(3)(d) limited the employee's TTD for soft tissue injury to eight weeks. The employee argued that § 22(3)(d) constituted "special legislation" because it classified part of this homogeneous group as non-surgical and thereby denied that class the right to claim TTD benefits beyond eight weeks. The court disagreed that this statute constituted "special legislation." Although § 22(3)(d) separated for different treatment under the statutory benefit scheme part of the entire class of employees with soft tissue injuries, employees with soft tissue injuries did not constitute a class "of similarly affected persons."


OUTCOME: The court vacated the TTD award and the denial of overpayment of TTD and directed the trial court to enter an order reflecting an overpayment of $ 2,477.85.

 

360 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Quinton v. Cherokee Nation Enters.


Case No. 107,128


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION FOUR


2010 OK CIV APP 16; 229 P.3d 581; 2009 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 130



December 18, 2009, Decided 
December 18, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals February 4, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING TO REVIEW AN ORDER OF A THREE-JUDGE PANEL OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT. HONORABLE RICHARD L. BLANCHARD, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant employee, a member of the Cherokee Nation, was injured during the course of his employment with a casino owned by respondent Cherokee Nation Enterprises (employer), and sought workers' compensation benefits. Respondent Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Court held that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction and a three-judge panel of that court affirmed. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee asserted that barring him from the Oklahoma workers' compensation courts violated his constitutional rights to equal protection and due process of law because the provisions of Oklahoma's Workers' Compensation Act were more favorable to workers than the provisions of the Cherokee Nation's Workers' Compensation Act. The court held that the employee's argument misunderstood the nature of sovereign immunity and its effect on an Oklahoma court's ability to entertain a private civil claim, regardless of its basis, against an employer. Here, the employer was an Indian tribe, a sovereign entity that had not waived its immunity from being sued in and subjected to the jurisdiction of Oklahoma courts, at least in the area of workers' compensation. Regardless of whether the employer's workers' compensation statutes treated employees better or worse than the Oklahoma workers' compensation statutes, an Oklahoma workers' compensation court lacked jurisdiction to hear the employee's claim because the employer had not consented to allowing such an action to be brought against it, which was the essence of sovereignty. The employee's forum was a tribal court.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the order.

 

361 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Frantz v. Drywall


Case Number: 106812


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2010 OK CIV APP 43; 233 P.3d 396; 2009 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 150



December 18, 2009, Decided 
April 15, 2010, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 5, 2010.

Released for Publication April 15, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MURRAY COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE JOHN H. SCAGGS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant benefits claimant challenged a decision from the District Court of Murray County, Oklahoma, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, an employer and its principal, in a dispute over the payment of a workers' compensation judgment entered against a professional employer organization (PEO) and its carrier.


OVERVIEW: After the claimant sustained a work-related injury, he filed a workers' compensation claim only against the PEO and its carrier. A workers' compensation court entered an award against the PEO and its carrier, and the judgments were certified after a default. Thereafter, the claimant filed a district court action against the employer, its principal, the PEO, and others. Summary judgment was granted in favor of the employer and its principal, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that both the PEO and its client (the employer) were considered employers for workers' compensation purposes, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 600.7(E) (2002). Under the exclusive remedy doctrine in Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 12 (2001), the employer and its principal were immune from tort liability in the district court. A first instance determination of workers' compensation liability in the proper forum was required to afford the employer and its principal due process. Moreover, judgments from the workers' compensation court were certified due to the default of the PEO. There was no payment obligation or default on the part of the employer or the principal.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

362 of 423 DOCUMENTS



Bank of Okla. v. Ashley


Case Number: 105270


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION FOUR


2009 OK CIV APP 50; 212 P.3d 507; 2009 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 28



April 16, 2009, Decided 
April 16, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals May 14, 2009. Mandate Issued: May 14, 2009. As Corrected June 10, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE CHARLES G. HUMBLE, TRIAL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant debtor appealed from a denial of the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, of her motion to release a judgment lien held by plaintiff bank.


OVERVIEW: The bank filed suit against the debtor in an underlying matter, and it obtained a default judgment. The bank recorded the judgment, and it properly perfected a judgment lien on the debtor's real property. Thereafter, the debtor and her husband filed for Chapter 7 bankruptcy protection. At issue on appeal was whether a pre-existing judgment lien on a debtor's real property survived a bankruptcy discharge in light of Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 706(E)(2) (2001). The appellate court noted that there was no evidence that the bank's pre-existing, valid judgment lien was disallowed or avoided. Therefore, under bankruptcy law it survived the debtor's discharge, and remained enforceable. Nevertheless, the debtor asserted that under state law, the judgment lien did not survive. The appellate court disagreed because a broad, literal reading of § 706(E)(2) would render it unconstitutional. The legislative intent of § 706(E)(2) was that judgments extinguished by bankruptcy proceedings no longer had vitality to attach as liens to real estate subsequently acquired by a debtor. The state statute did not apply to valid liens existing at the time the debtor filed her bankruptcy petition.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.


 

363 of 423 DOCUMENTS



City of Edmond v. Vernon


Case Number: 105820


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION FOUR


2009 OK CIV APP 36; 210 P.3d 860; 2008 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 127



December 22, 2008, Decided 
December 22, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Certiorari to Court of Appeals Denied March 30, 2009. This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals April 10, 2009. Mandate Issued: April 10, 2009. As Corrected May 5, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING TO REVIEW AN ORDER OF A THREE-JUDGE PANEL OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT. HONORABLE GENE PRIGMORE, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city sought review of an order of a three-judge panel of respondent, the Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Court (WCC), affirming an award of benefits to respondent claimant. The WCC found that the city failed to overcome the presumption of Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 49-110(A) (Supp. 2008), that the claimant's colon cancer arose out of and in the course of employment as a firefighter with the city.


OVERVIEW: The city asserted that § 49-110(A) violated various constitutional provisions. On review, the court sustained the WCC's determination. The court concluded that § 49-110(A) did not violate Okla. Const. art. 5, § 46, because the statutory presumption was based on a reasonable legislative classification, such classification had a reasonable relationship to the express purposes of the Worker's Compensation Act and public policy, and the claim of municipal firefighters had distinctive characteristics upon which different treatment could be reasonably founded. Although § 49-110 was a special law, with no applicable general law, it did not violate Okla. Const. art. 5, § 59, because the legislature was entitled to determine that firefighters were particularly vulnerable to exposure to disease-causing smoke and hazardous chemicals, making the presumption related to a valid objective. Additionally, the city failed to show that the statute violated procedural due process because the claimant filed for compensation and the city had access to the courts. Finally, competent evidence supported the WCC's decision that the city failed to rebut the statutory presumption.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the determination of the WCC.


 

364 of 423 DOCUMENTS



Lester v. Smith


Case Number: 104854


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2008 OK CIV APP 97; 198 P.3d 402; 2008 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 73



July 11, 2008, Decided 
November 13, 2008, Mandate Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE J. MICHAEL GASSETT, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff home buyers brought an action against defendant sellers in the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, claiming a right of recovery under § 837 of the Oklahoma Residential Property Condition Disclosure Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 60, § 831 et seq. The trial court granted summary judgment to the sellers based on § 837(C)'s two-year limitation period, and the buyers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The buyers alleged that the sellers disclosed certain foundation problems but denied knowledge of water seepage and additional problems prior to closing of the sale in March 2004. They brought their action in April 2007. Under Okla. Stat. tit. 60, § 837(C), an action under the Act was required to be brought within two years. The buyers argued that the discovery rule applied to toll the two-year period. The court held that § 837(C) was a statute of repose, not a statute of limitation, based on its language, which not only barred any causes of action then existing, but, at the running of the respective limitation periods, had the effect of preventing what otherwise might be a cause of action from ever arising. Because it was a statute of repose, the discovery rule did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the sellers.


 

365 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Harrison v. Morgan


Case Number: 104342


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2008 OK CIV APP 68; 191 P.3d 617; 2008 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 49



June 20, 2008, Decided 
June 20, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals July 25, 2008. Mandate Issued: July 25, 2008. As Corrected July 25, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TEXAS COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE RYAN D. REDDICK, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed a judgment of the District Court of Texas County (Oklahoma) denying him permission to relocate with the parties' children in his custody over the objection of petitioner mother.


OVERVIEW: The father was granted sole custody with visitation rights to the mother. The father gave timely notice of his intent to relocate with the children, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 43, § 112.3 (2002), and the mother objected. The court held that a decision to relocate a family rested within the custodial parent's authority subject to the trial court's approval, where the custodial parent was fit and there was no risk of real and specific harm to the children. The court held that the trial court did not properly apply the factors set forth in Okla. Stat. tit. 43, § 112.3(J)(1)(a)-(g) (2002) and had given undue weight to several factors including the effect of the relocation on the mother's visitation schedule and on the parties' finances. The trial court also erred in not considering an alternative visitation plan that would allow the relocation. The weight of the factors in favor of relocation were greater than the weight of the factors against relocation. The court also held that the mother did not sustain her burden of demonstrating that the proposed relocation was contrary to the children's best interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to deny the mother's request to modify custody, reversed the trial court's decision on the relocation issue, and remanded for modification of visitation orders.

 

366 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Public Supply Co. v. Steenbock


Case Number: 104265


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2008 OK CIV APP 53; 186 P.3d 263; 2008 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 27



April 25, 2008, Decided 
April 25, 2008, Filed.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals May 22, 2008. Mandate Issued: May 22, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING TO REVIEW AN ORDER OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT. HONORABLE CHERRI FARRAR, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer appealed an order from a workers' compensation trial court (Oklahoma) which awarded appellee employee more than eight weeks of temporary total disability (TTD) benefits, arguing the order was in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 22 (3)(d) (2006).


OVERVIEW: The appeal raised the single issue of whether recent amendments to the workers' compensation laws regarding the award of benefits for a soft tissue injury reflected a legislative intent to limit those benefits to eight (8) weeks under the facts of the case. The court held that they did not. A claimant seeking TTD benefits for a soft tissue injury under Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 22(2)(c) (2006) could, upon proper proof, be entitled to those benefits listed therein for a maximum of three hundred (300) weeks. A claimant's TTD award was in no way limited by the provisions of § 22(3)(d), which only applied when a claimant was seeking permanent partial disability (PPD) benefits for a "Soft Tissue Injury" as that injury was defined in § 22(3)(d). When a claimant reached maximum medical improvement, or was otherwise no longer considered to be temporarily totally disabled, and sought PPD benefits, such claimant could seek, in addition to his § 22(2)(c) TTD benefits, PPD benefits for a soft tissue injury. There was no error in the trial court's award of TTD benefits to the employee under § 22(2)(c), as it was not limited to the benefits set out for PPD under § 22(3)(d).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court.

 

367 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Integris Baptist Med. Ctr.


Case Number: 103640


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2008 OK CIV APP 14; 178 P.3d 191; 2008 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 1



January 10, 2008, Decided 
January 10, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected February 7, 2008. This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals February 7, 2008. Mandate Issued: February 7, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE BARBARA G. SWINTON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administratrix brought a wrongful death action against defendant health care providers. The District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) dismissed the action on the grounds that: (1) a previous action was deemed dismissed pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 150; and (2) the new action had not been brought within one year of the §150 "deemed" dismissal and was thus time-barred under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 100. The administratrix appealed.


OVERVIEW: Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 150 provided that in a medical liability action, a summons was to be served on the defendants within 180 days of the filing of the lawsuit, or the case was to be deemed dismissed without prejudice. The administratrix challenge the validity of §150 as an impermissible special law in violation of Okla. Const. art. V, § 46. The court agreed, noting that: (1) art. V, § 46 required that court procedure apply equally across the board for an entire class of similarly situated persons; (2) Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2004(I) (Supp. 2002) permitted dismissal of an action if an ordinary plaintiff failed to obtain service of summons within 180 days of issuance, but required notice to an ordinary plaintiff, either by the court or by the movant on a motion to dismiss; and (3) Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 150, with its "deemed dismissed" provision, afforded a medical negligence plaintiff no such notice prior to dismissal, and prior notice of proceedings affecting one's rights were at the core of due process protections. Because the new action was commenced within one year of the filing of the trial court's order of dismissal, the action was timely under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 100.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order of dismissal was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

368 of 423 DOCUMENTS


G.E. Capital Info. Tech. Solutions, Inc. v. Okla. City Pub. Schs


Case Number: 103213


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2007 OK CIV APP 116; 173 P.3d 114; 2007 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 90



November 1, 2007, Decided 
November 30, 2007, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 30, 2007 [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE NOMA D. GURICH, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school district appealed the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff company, on the company's petition to collect balances due on lease agreements for photocopying machines and related equipment and services, and awarding the company $ 263,648 in damages, plus attorney fees and costs.


OVERVIEW: The school district did not dispute that employees at various schools signed the lease agreements. The school district, however, denied that its board of education was aware of or had ever approved or ratified the leases, and denied that the board of education authorized any payments on the leases or that the applicable statutory accounting procedures had been followed. The school district also argued that because the leases did not contain the requisite contractual provision for mutual ratification of renewal pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 70, § 5-117(B) (Supp. 2006), the lease agreements were void and unenforceable. The school district returned only six of the thirteen copiers and was unable to locate the remaining copiers. The appellate court ruled that use of the leased property, payment, and acceptance of payment during any fiscal year constituted mutual ratification of renewal. However, it was error for the trial court to assess damages against the school district based on the automatic month-to-month renewal provisions in the leases for holdover rents for a period beyond the lease term to the date of trial.


OUTCOME: The portion of the judgment concerning the amount of damages awarded to the company was reversed and remanded, the portion of the judgment concerning the amount of attorney fees was reversed and remanded, and the judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

369 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Fancy's Entm't L.L.C. v. City of Enid


Case Number: 103588


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2007 OK CIV APP 112; 171 P.3d 928; 2007 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 85



October 23, 2007, Decided 
November 15, 2007, Mandate Issued 
November 15, 2007, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GARFIELD COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE MARK A. MOORE, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an adult low-point beer establishment and an employee and patrons of the establishment, sued defendant city, challenging the validity of a city ordinance making it illegal for persons under 21 to enter a low-point beer establishment that allowed persons to perform or work in a nearly nude state. The District Court of Garfield County (Oklahoma) granted the city summary judgment. The establishment and its employee and patrons appealed.


OVERVIEW: Holding the ordinance invalid, the court noted that Okla. Stat. Ann. tit. 37, §§ 241(B) (2001) (amended 2006), 243 (2001), and 246 (2001) (amended 2006) permitted 18- to 20-year-old patrons and employees to enter a low-point beer establishment if the establishment segregated the area in which low-point beer was sold and did not allow such patrons to enter that area. In contrast, the ordinance denied entry to 20 year-old service workers even when the services were performed while the establishment was closed, precluded the establishment's hiring of 20-year-old employees even though the employment of such persons in such establishments was permitted by state law, and denied entry to 18- to 20-year-old patrons who did not enter the designated bar area even though they were specifically permitted to enter that area by state law. Although Okla. Stat. Ann. tit. 37, § 219 (2001) authorized municipalities to enact ordinances prohibiting or regulating nudity or drink solicitation in low-point beer establishments, this general grant of authority did not authorize a city to regulate the age of admission to such establishments in a manner inconsistent with specific Oklahoma statutes.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was reversed.

 

370 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tambunga (In re S.A.)


Case Number: 104333


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2007 OK CIV APP 97; 169 P.3d 730; 2007 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 70



September 7, 2007, Decided 
October 5, 2007, Mandate Issued 
October 5, 2007Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GARFIELD COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE TOM NEWBY, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent State obtained an adjudication that the children were deprived and later sought to terminate appellant parents' parental rights. A jury found the parents failed to correct the conditions leading to the deprived adjudication, and the children had been in foster care for 15 of the most recent 22 months. Based on these findings, the District Court of Garfield County, Oklahoma, terminated the parents' parental rights. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the parents contended the trial court failed to order specific conditions they had to correct in order to be reunited with the children; they also asserted that they were not at fault for the length of time the children remained in foster care. The appellate court disagreed with the parents' assertion that termination was based on their failure to complete the plan; the jury found that they failed to correct the conditions leading to the deprived adjudication, as required by statute before terminating parental rights. The evidence leading to removal showed that the parents home was not safe for the children: the parents neglected the children's basic hygiene needs as well as their needs to be safe from physical harm, and exposed the children to domestic violence. The record also showed that the parents received trial court-approved individual treatment plans which explained the conditions, and clear and convincing evidence showed that they failed to correct those conditions. Further, the parents did not assert that the State or treatment providers thwarted their ability to correct those conditions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

371 of 423 DOCUMENTS


City of Stillwater v. Oliver


Case Number: 103728


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2007 OK CIV APP 62; 164 P.3d 1149; 2007 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 35



May 23, 2007, Decided 
June 22, 2007, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals June 22, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING TO REVIEW AN ORDER OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT. HONORABLE RICHARD L. BLANCHARD, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer, a city, sought review of an order of the Workers' Compensation Court which found that respondent employee, a firefighter, sustained an accidental injury to the lumbar spine, arising out of and in the course of employment. The employer argued that the trial court erred in applying Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 17(A) (Supp. 2005) to exclude its witnesses' testimony and that § 17(A) was an unconstitutional delegation of authority.


OVERVIEW: The trial court abused its discretion and erred as a matter of law in excluding relevant evidence proffered by the employer. The employer's offer of proof, which the trial court refused to hear, indicated that eyewitness testimony would have addressed the issue of whether the employee in fact engaged in the activity he claimed caused his injury. The employer asserted that the statute, on which the trial court relied to exclude the evidence, was unconstitutional. The record did not present a question of constitutionality. The trial court interpreted § 17 to mean that once the treating physician established injury causation, the employer could only rebut the presumption of compensability by seeking an independent medical examination. The trial court refused to hear any testimony from the employer's causation witnesses who would have testified that the employee had no contact nor participated in the alleged treatment and carrying of an accident victim. The trial court abused its discretion in excluding evidence directly relevant to the essential issue of whether the employee in fact sustained an injury arising out of and in the course of employment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order and remanded for a retrial of the employee's claim.

 

372 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Franks v. Noble


Case Number: 103753


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2007 OK CIV APP 39; 159 P.3d 302; 2007 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 13



April 6, 2007, Decided  
May 3, 2007, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication by Order of the Supreme Court of Oklahoma May 3, 2007.
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHEROKEE COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE JEFF PAYTON, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant purported owner challenged a decision from the District Court of Cherokee County (Oklahoma), which granted summary judgment to appellee purported owners in an action seeking to quiet title in property.


OVERVIEW: When taxes on certain property became delinquent, a county treasurer sent notices to the persons listed on the tax rolls. Two envelopes were returned unsigned, but they provided a forwarding address. No notice was provided to other people with an interest in the property. The land was eventually sold at a tax sale, and it was later inherited by appellant. She sought to quiet titled in the property, but summary judgment was granted to appellees. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court held that the county treasurer was required to exercise due diligence in sending notice under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 3106 (2001). In addition, there was a due process requirement under the Fourteenth Amendment regarding notice. This constitutional requirement was violated when not all persons with an interest in the property received notice. As to the returned envelopes, the county treasurer had the duty to follow up under the Fourteenth Amendment and under the statutory due diligence requirement when forwarding addresses were provided. Publication did not cure the defects either. Due to the fact that the tax deed was void, appellant did not have title to the property.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Panhandle Producers & Royalty Owners Ass'n v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


Case Number: 104002


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2007 OK CIV APP 68; 162 P.3d 960; 2007 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 42



March 28, 2007, Decided 
July 19, 2007, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals. Approved for Publication by the Supreme Court.
Writ of certiorari denied, Ordered published by Panhandle Producers & Royalty Owners Ass'n v. Okla. Tax Comm'n, 2007 OK 62, 2007 Okla. LEXIS 129 (Okla., 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Panhandle Producers & Royalty Owners Ass'n v. Okla. Tax Comm'n, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12842 (U.S., Dec. 3, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE DANIEL L. OWENS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an owners' association and a corporation, sought a declaratory judgment to declare a statute unconstitutional that required operators to withhold income tax from oil and gas royalty payments made to royalty interest owners who did not reside in Oklahoma. The association also sought an injunction. Summary judgment was granted to defendant Oklahoma Tax Commission (OTC). The association and the corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The association was a trade association that represented royalty owners in three states. The cause of action arose out of the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the United States Constitution. At issue in this case was the constitutionality of an Oklahoma statute requiring operators to withhold income tax from oil and gas royalty payments made to royalty interest owners who do not reside in Oklahoma. The withholding statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2385.26 (Supp. 2006), was a method of collecting taxes which did not increase the actual tax burden on nonresidents. Additionally, OTC had shown a rational basis for the classification in the statute. The collection method had only an incidental effect on interstate commerce, which was outweighed by OTC's interest in collecting taxes before the income leaves the state. The statute passed constitutional muster, and OTC was entitled to judgment as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

Libertarian Political Org. v. Clingman


Case Number: 103592


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION FOUR


2007 OK CIV APP 51; 162 P.3d 948; 2007 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 23



February 27, 2007, Decided 
May 25, 2007, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE BRYAN C. DIXON, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a political organization, members, and officers, sued defendants, the Oklahoma State Election Board and officials, alleging that Oklahoma's ballot access laws regarding formation and recognition of a political party were unconstitutional. The District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) granted summary judgment in favor of defendants and denied plaintiffs' request for a declaratory judgment. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that the state's ballot access requirements were unduly restrictive and unconstitutionally interfered with their association rights under the Oklahoma Constitution and the First and Fourteenth Amendments to the U.S. Constitution. Plaintiffs asserted that state law, including Okla. Stat. tit. 26, § 1-108 (Supp. 2006), required them to collect an unduly burdensome number of voter signatures on the petition, all within too short a period of time. The appellate court determined that § 1-108 did not violate plaintiffs' constitutional rights because the statute did not unnecessarily restrict or infringe upon the associational rights of plaintiffs, and was reasonable and justified by legitimate state interests. The restrictions regarding the time period and the number of signatures were not unreasonable, severe, or discriminatory, because, inter alia, the party had been able to place the name of its presidential candidate on the ballot, using essentially the same procedure, on two previous occasions, and the evidentiary material affirmatively suggested that plaintiffs did not make reasonable efforts to collect the required signatures.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's order.

State ex rel. Dugger v. Twelve Thousand Dollars Cash


Case Number: 98995


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2007 OK CIV APP 20; 155 P.3d 858; 2007 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 5



January 30, 2007, Decided  
February 22, 2007, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Appeals February 22, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BECKHAM COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE DOUG HAUGHT, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to the Enforcement and Administrative Provisions of the Uniform Controlled Dangerous Substances Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 63, §§ 2-501 to 2-511 (2001), appellee county district attorney filed a petition seeking forfeiture of cash confiscated from appellant claimant's rental vehicle. The District Court of Beckham County (Oklahoma) denied the claimant's request for a jury trial and granted the forfeiture request. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: As a result of a stop for speeding, the claimant was arrested on suspicion of drug trafficking and $ 12,000 in cash was confiscated from the rental vehicle. The county district attorney sought forfeiture of the cash, alleging that the cash was intended to be used to purchase marijuana. The appellate court determined that the trial court's finding that there was nothing in the language of Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-506 (2001) that specifically required a jury trial was reasonable. Also, the claimant's assertion of a Seventh Amendment right to jury trial failed because the Seventh Amendment's guarantee of a jury trial in civil forfeiture cases was not applicable to the states. However, the trial court erred in denying the claimant's request for a jury trial because trial by jury in civil cases involving more than $ 1,500 was guaranteed by Okla. Const. art. 2, § 19, and that constitutional guarantee applied in forfeiture proceedings of property that was not contraband per se conducted pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-506.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

Gee v. All 4 Kids, Inc.


No. 103,161


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2006 OK CIV APP 155; 149 P.3d 1106; 2006 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 136



November 21, 2006, Decided  
December 20, 2006, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals December 20, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING TO REVIEW AN ORDER OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT. HONORABLE KENTON W. FULTON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner benefits claimant challenged a decision from respondent Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Court, which awarded her only 8 weeks of temporary total disability (TTD) benefits for a back injury suffered at respondent employer's workplace.


OVERVIEW: The claimant suffered a soft tissue injury to her back. She was awarded 8 weeks of TTD benefits, despite medical evidence that it had continued for longer. This appeal followed. In vacating the award, the appellate court rejected the claimant's arguments under Okla. Const. art. II, §§ 6, 7. The claimant had no vested right in any particular workers' compensation remedy prior to the injury, and §§ 6, 7 did not place a limitation on the Oklahoma Legislature's power to restrict the benefits recoverable for soft tissue injuries. Therefore, the claimant's due process rights and right to a certain remedy had not been violated. However, there was a conflict in Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 22 with regards to TTD benefits for soft tissue injuries. The 8-week limit in § 22(3)(d) clearly conflicted with the 300-week limit in § 22(2)(c). The appellate court used the rules of statutory construction to determine that the reference of § 22(3) to § 22(2) controlled. Therefore, § 22(2) permitted an aggregate award of up to 300 weeks of TTD in a soft tissue case.


OUTCOME: The decision was vacated, and the case was remanded for an award of TTD consistent with the medical evidence and the statutory interpretation on appeal.

 

377 of 423 DOCUMENTS


In re Assessments for the Year 2003 of Certain Props. Owned by Affordable Residential Cmtys. 7, L.L.C. v. Canadian County Assessor


Case No. 101,603


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2006 OK CIV APP 147; 150 P.3d 399; 2006 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 135



November 14, 2006, Decided  
December 8, 2006, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals, December 8, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CANADIAN COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE GARY E. MILLER, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers, appealed a judgment of the District Court of Canadian County (Oklahoma), which granted summary judgment to respondent county assessor, upholding its valuation of taxpayers' property in the taxpayers' action seeking review of and a reduction in the assessments that were allegedly in excess of five percent, a violation of Okla. Const. art. X, § 8B.


OVERVIEW: The title to the properties were transferred from entities owned and controlled by the parent corporation to other entities owned and controlled by the parent corporation, which included the taxpayers, and the assessor increased the assessment on the taxpayers' properties. The trial court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2802.1(A)(4)(g) did not contemplate such a conveyance of properties. On appeal, the court found that § 2802.1(A)(4)(g) was constitutional. Okla. Const. art. X, § 8B required the legislature to define the material terms and to enact the laws necessary to implement its provisions. All property remained on the tax rolls and was subject to ad valorem taxation. Only the property's increase in value in excess of five percent was capped and not assessed. In transferring the deeds between entities owned by the parent corporation, it retained control and ownership over the properties. Pursuant to § 8B, the properties' fair cash values could not be increased by more than five percent, and the trial court erred in determining otherwise.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the action to the trial court with instructions to the trial court to enter judgment to the taxpayers on its motion for summary judgment.

Thales Navigation, Inc. v. Tulsa County


Case No. 103,534


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2006 OK CIV APP 154; 149 P.3d 1103; 2006 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 127



November 3, 2006, Decided  
December 8, 2006, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] This Opinion has been Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals, December 8, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE RONALD L. SHAFFER, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee corporate taxpayer brought suit against appellant county tax assessor challenging the denial of its request for a refund of ad valorem taxes and penalties paid on personal property it claimed was exempt from taxation; appellant State intervened. The District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, granted the taxpayer's motion for summary judgment. The assessor and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the assessor and the State argued that the trial court erred in ruling that Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2902.2 (2001) was unconstitutional. The appellate court found that the trial court properly determined that the taxpayer was entitled to a refund of the ad valorem taxes paid on its constitutionally exempt property. Because the freeport exemption under Okla. Const. art. X, § 6A was self-executing, the tax assessed on the taxpayer's property was illegal and void. However, the trial court's determination was based on its erroneous legal conclusion that Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2902.2 (2001) was unconstitutional because the March 15 deadline nullified the freeport exemption; § 2902.2 was not unconstitutional. Because the taxpayer did not file its list by the March 15 deadline, it was delinquent, and it suffered a statutory penalty pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2836(C) (2001). Even though the taxpayer filed past the deadline, it was still entitled to the exemption, but had to pay the penalty.


OUTCOME: That portion of the summary judgment ordering a refund of ad valorem taxes paid on constitutionally exempt property was affirmed; that portion of the summary judgment ordering a refund of the penalties paid on the property was reversed and remanded to the trial court for a proper determination of the correct penalty amount.

Pub. Serv. Co. v. B. Willis, C.P.A.


Case Number: 101,557


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2007 OK CIV APP 18; 155 P.3d 845; 2006 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 152



September 19, 2006, Decided  
February 16, 2007, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
This Opinion is Released for Publication by Order of the Court of Civil Appeals February 5, 2007
Writ of certiorari denied, Ordered published by Public Serv. Co. v. Willis, 2007 Okla. LEXIS 14 (Okla., Feb. 5, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by B. Willis, C.P.A., Inc. v. Pub. Serv. Co., 552 U.S. 813, 128 S. Ct. 66, 169 L. Ed. 2d 16, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 10314 (2007)
Related proceeding at B. Willis, C.P.A., Inc. v. BNSF Ry. Corp., 531 F.3d 1282, 2008 U.S. App. LEXIS 15118 (10th Cir. Okla., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF ROGERS COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE JAMES D. GOODPASTER, TRIAL JUDGE.
Public Serv. Co. v. B. Willis, C.P.A., 1997 OK 78, 941 P.2d 995, 1997 Okla. LEXIS 76 (Okla., 1997)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Public Service Company of Oklahoma (PSO) brought a condemnation proceeding against defendant property owner under Okla. Stat. tit. 66, §§ 51-60 (1991), seeking an easement for the construction of a railroad. On remand, the District Court of Rogers County (Oklahoma) denied the property owner's motion to dismiss, overruled the property owner's objection to a report of commissioners, and ruled in favor of PSO. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that PSO had established that its condemnation of the property owner's property was for a public use and was reasonably necessary. The property owner argued that the "date of take" used for the valuation of his property was in error because, although his property was valued as of December 28, 1992, the date the commissioners filed their report, PSO's right to condemn was not established until November 15, 2004, when the trial court entered the order. The appellate court rejected the property owner's argument because (1) under Okla. Const. art. 2, § 24 and Okla. Stat. tit. 66, § 56 (2001), the payment of the award to the court clerk authorized PSO to enter onto the property and construct its rail spur regardless of his subsequent appeal, and (2) there was sufficient evidence to support the trial court's ruling that the rail spur construction constituted a public use justifying condemnation. The property owner's argument that federal preemption applied was precluded by an adverse ruling he obtained from the Surface Transportation Board. Ample evidence supported the conclusion that PSO lawfully exercised its power of eminent domain in condemning the property.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.

 

380 of 423 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Lane v. Seven Hundred Twenty Five Dollars


Case No. 101,756


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2006 OK CIV APP 74; 136 P.3d 1076; 2006 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 41



May 16, 2006, Decided  
June 16, 2006, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE BRYAN C. DIXON, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant challenged a decision from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which denied his motion to vacate a default judgment ordering the forfeiture of $725 to appellee State.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a forfeiture action to obtain money found in a car near drugs, and notice was provided in three ways. In 2000, a default judgment was granted to the State because the claimant failed to answer. In 2004, the claimant filed a motion to vacate the default judgment. The request was denied, and the claimant sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion. The record showed no due process violation because the claimant was provided with service of process, and he failed to respond within the 45 day period under Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-506(D) (Rev. Supp. 2005). Next, the State's act of providing the arresting officer's affidavit setting out the factual basis of the forfeiture request constituted a prima facie showing of the nexus between the drugs and the money found in close proximity. The burden then shifted to the claimant to rebut the showing, but he chose not to answer. As such, his arguments concerning lack of evidence failed. Finally, the claimant's request was time barred under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1038, and Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 06 (2001) did not provide for incarceration as a disability.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

381 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Simic v. State ex rel. Dep't of Pub. Safety


Case No. 102,386


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2006 OK CIV APP 8; 129 P.3d 177; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 110



December 30, 2005, Decided  
January 27, 2006, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 27, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF PAYNE COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE DONALD L. WORTHINGTON, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the District Court of Payne County, Oklahoma that denied defendant's denied defendant's motion to quash and sustained a decision by the Department of Public Safety (DPS) revoking defendant's driver's license under Oklahoma's "implied consent" statutes, Okla. Stat. tit. 47, §§ 751 through 754 (2001 & Supp. 2005). Defendant claimed his arrest was invalid because the campus police officer was outside his jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the campus officer was outside his jurisdiction; but the trial court upheld the validity of the arrest because defendant committed an "offense" in the officer's presence; therefore the officer was entitled to effect a "citizen's arrest" under Okla. Stat. tit. 22 § 202 (2001). On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred to the extent it found that, even if the campus officer was outside his jurisdiction, he nonetheless made a valid "citizen's arrest" because a campus police officer may not make an arrest outside school property while acting in the capacity of a campus police officer. However, the court held that the officer's arrest was valid because the officer was within his jurisdiction where the city and the university had entered into an agreement that extended jurisdiction of campus police officers to property surrounding and adjacent to the campus. The court held that such agreements were specifically authorized by the Oklahoma Campus Security Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 74, §§ 360.15 through 360.21 (2001), and that the circumstances of the case fell squarely within those contemplated by the city and university agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order.

 

382 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Save Ad Valorem Funding for Students v. Okla. Dep't of Envtl. Quality


Case No. 102,678


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2006 OK CIV APP 53; 135 P.3d 823; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 135



December 23, 2005, Decided  
April 28, 2006, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication by order of the Supreme Court April 17, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE PATRICIA G. PARRISH, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school funding association challenged a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) that determined Okla. Stat. tit. 68, §§ 2817(E) and 2817.3 (2004) were constitutional in its suit against appellees, Oklahoma Department of Environmental Quality (DEQ), county assessor, Oklahoma Tax Commission (OTC), State Board of Equalization (SBOE), and an oil refinery, seeking a declaration that the statutes were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The association challenged the trial court's findings. On appeal, the court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 68, §§ 2817(E) and 2817.3 (2004) were unconstitutional. The court found that the statutes violated Okla. Const. art. V, § 50; Okla. Const. art. X, § 22; and Okla. Const. art. X, § 8. The court found that without using the language of an exemption, Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2817(E) directed the assessor to exclude the value of desulphurization equipment from the valuation of an oil refinery's property and Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2817.3 implemented Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2817(E) by providing a procedure to apply for "exclusion" of the property. By withdrawing the desulphurization equipment from ad valorem taxation, the statutes created an ad valorem tax exemption, yet they did not provide a substitute tax as required by Okla. Const. art. V, § 50, and Okla. Const. art. X, § 22, and because the statutes allowed refineries taxed ad valorem to be assessed at less than 10 % of its fair cash value without the voters' approval, they violated Okla. Const. art. X, § 8. The court also noted that the exemption did not qualify under Okla. Const. art. X, § 6B and Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2902.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment and remanded the case with instructions to enter judgment in favor of the association. The court denied the association's motion for oral argument and the submission of briefs.

Rocket Oil & Gas Co. v. Donabar


Case No. 99,644


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2005 OK CIV APP 111; 127 P.3d 625; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 99; 162 Oil & Gas Rep. 708



November 28, 2005, Decided  
December 23, 2005, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication: December 23, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF PUSHMATAHA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE GARY BROCK, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant trustee sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Pushmataha County (Oklahoma), which quieted title in favor of plaintiffs, an oil and gas company, a revocable trust, an exploration company, three other companies, and an individual, to the minerals underlying a certain property. The trial court found that plaintiffs had an unbroken chain of title under the Marketable Record Title Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 16, § 71 et seq. (2001).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed based on different reasons. The court first rejected the trustee's arguments based on after-acquired title or estoppel by deed. The court next determined that a 1929 mineral deed was the "root of title" in plaintiffs' chain of record title, 40 years after the filing of which plaintiffs could rely for establishing marketable record title (MRT) in the minerals under the subject property, unless plaintiffs' MRT was subject to other "interests or defects" excepted from application of the Act by Okla. Stat. tit. 16, § 72 (2001). The court determined there was no "interest or defects" excepted by § 72. Finally, the court rejected the trustee's claim that the MRTA was unconstitutional. It required the trustee's predecessor in interest, after the filing of the mineral deeds in plaintiffs' chain of title, to perform reasonable conditions to demonstrate his intention to retain his minerals; either file a Okla. Stat. tit. 16, § 74(a) (2001) notice or other "title transaction" or be in "continuous possession" as defined by § 74(b). He did not do that, and a 1971 warranty deed in the trustee's chain of title was filed too late to preserve the pre-root interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

384 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Bruner v. State ex rel. Okla. Tax Comm'n (In re Gross Prod. & Petroleum Excise Tax Protest)


Case No. 100,536


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2006 OK CIV APP 21; 130 P.3d 767; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 120; 169 Oil & Gas Rep. 203



September 20, 2005, Decided  
March 3, 2006, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 9, 2006.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bruner v. Ok, ex rel. Ok Tax Comm'n, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5766 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM ORDER OF THE OKLAHOMA TAX COMMISSION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission (OTC) entered a judgment, finding appellant taxpayer's application for a tax refund barred in part by a statute of limitations. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed an application with the OTC seeking refund of gross production and petroleum excise taxes paid. The taxes were imposed pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1008 (1994) and Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1106 (2001). The taxpayer claimed that the oil production was from restricted Indian land he had inherited. The question on appeal was whether Oklahoma had authority to levy these taxes on oil and gas produced from restricted Indian land. The taxpayer argued that the Act of May 10, 1928, was unconstitutional as applied to him because he had a vested right to an exemption from taxation applicable to his grandfather's allotment of 1903. He also argued that the collection of the illegal tax was a breach of fiduciary duty. The appellate court noted that the agreements between the United States and the Muscogee (Creek) Nation did not provide for perpetual taxation exemptions. The 21-year tax exemption provided under the Original and Supplemental Creek Agreements expired well before Congress enacted the Act of May 10, 1928. A continuation of restrictions on alienation of land did not continue the taxation exemption. The provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2373 did not apply.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

Anderson Mech., Inc. v. Spiegel


No. 101,195


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2005 OK CIV APP 60; 119 P.3d 1287; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 47



August 4, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: August 31, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING TO REVIEW AN ORDER OF A THREE-JUDGE PANEL OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT.



DISPOSITION: SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing respondent insurance company and denying petitioner employer's motion to add a previous insurer as a party-respondent in respondent employee's claim for workers' compensation. The employer and petitioner insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employer and the insurer argued that the employee became aware of his job-related injuries in May 2000 when he first received medical treatment for those injuries, and that the law in effect at the time of the employee's awareness of his job-related injuries controlled the rights and obligations of the parties. The appellate court found that under Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 11(B)(5), the law then in effect at the time the insurer assumed the risk, and the law in effect at the time of the employee's last hazardous exposure in his single employment, the insurer on the risk on the last day of exposure was solely liable where the claimant worked for a single employer for the 90 days prior to last exposure. The employee worked only for the employer over the last 24 years, during which he was last hazardously exposed to the repetitive-trauma dealing conditions of that employment for more than 90 days, and the insurer was the insurance carrier on the last day of the employee's exposure. Pursuant to the statute, the insurer was consequently liable for payment of the employee's benefits.


OUTCOME: The order was sustained.

 

386 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Superior Bronze & Granite of Am. v. Cole


No. 101,044


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2005 OK CIV APP 55; 118 P.3d 778; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 42; 76 O.B.A.J. 1888



July 8, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released For Publication: August 11, 2005.



DISPOSITION: SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an employer and its insurance carrier, filed an action to obtain review of a decision of the three-judge panel of the Workers' Compensation Court (Oklahoma), which affirmed the trial court's order adjudicating respondent claimant a physically impaired person who was permanently disabled as a result of combined disabilities and which held the employer liable for an increased disability under Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 172(B)(2).


OVERVIEW: The workers' compensation trial court adjudicated claimant as having a permanent total disability (PTD) arising from the combination of the pre-existing disabilities and the disability attributable to the claimant's latest work-related injury and held the employer liable for the payment of the PTD. The trial court also determined that vocational rehabilitation was not practicable. The three-judge panel affirmed all findings, with a modification on the compensation rate. The court rejected the employer's contention that the amended version of Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 172, which became effective in May 2000, violated the employer's rights under the U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and U.S. Const. amend. V and XIV because it shifted liability away from the state-operated Multiple Injury Trust Fund. The employer did not have any vested rights in having the Fund pay a portion of the PTD when claimant's last injury occurred after the effective date of the amendment to Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 172. It was not error for the trial court to conclude that vocational rehabilitation was not practical based on the claimant's testimony and evidence and the report of the vocational rehabilitation expert.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the order of the three judge panel of the workers' compensation court.

Keco, Inc. v. Hayward


Case No. 100,925


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2005 OK CIV APP 53; 123 P.3d 50; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 40; 76 O.B.A.J. 1724



June 30, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] THIS OPINION HAS BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION BY ORDER OF THE COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS.
Released for Publication: July 28, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING TO REVIEW AND ORDER OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT. HONORABLE JIM FILOSA, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Court held petitioner insurer solely responsible for cumulative trauma injuries to the left hand/thumb of respondent employee and dismissed respondent insurance company, predecessor in interest to the Oklahoma Property and Casualty Insurance Guaranty Association (OPCIGA). The insurer and petitioner employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners argued that the trial court erred in dismissing the insurance company and holding the insurer solely liable for the employee's injuries under Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 11(B)(5). The appellate court found that it was undisputed that the employee suffered a cumulative trauma injury while working for the employer, and, although aware of the injury in March 2000, was last exposed to the cumulative trauma dealing hazards of the employment in August 2002. From and after the effective date of § 11(B)(5), the employee's "awareness" of his cumulative trauma injury was irrelevant to the determination of the "date of injury," by force of that section, determined solely by reference to the date of last exposure. The insurer assumed the risk on or about March 1, 2002, over a year after the effective date of the statute and was charged with notice of the law then in effect. The insurer suffered no increased obligation to pay greater benefits than when it assumed the risk.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

388 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Dollar Gen. Corp. v. Instaff Pers.


Case No. 101,783


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2005 OK CIV APP 86; 123 P.3d 45; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 71



June 17, 2005, Decided  
November 3, 2005, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication: November 03, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING TO REVIEW AN ORDER OF A THREE-JUDGE PANEL OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT.



DISPOSITION: SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer one denied respondent employee's claim for a cumulative trauma injury. The employee was found to have sustained a compensable injury and the employer was ordered to pay for medical treatment. Employer one's request to join respondents, employers two and three, was granted, but it was found solely liable for the employee's benefits. A three judge panel of the Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Court affirmed. Employer one appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, employer one challenged the trial court's finding that it was solely liable for the employee's injury and argued that Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 11(B)(5) (2001) was unconstitutional. The appellate court found that it was uncontroverted that the employee was employed by employer one for a period in excess of 90 days, and that during that period he was exposed to injury causing trauma, even though he was only actually working three, 12-hour workdays a week. This was sufficient to satisfy § 11(B)(5). The appellate court also looked to prior cases which addressed the constitutionality of § 11(B)(5) and agreed that it was neither arbitrary nor capricious, and had a rational relationship to a permissible public goal. The rule of imposing sole liability on the last employer satisfied two problems associated with cumulative trauma cases, i.e., proof and assignment of responsibility; assignment of responsibility to the last employer satisfied a "rational basis test" because it provided a definite measure of relief to the worker. As such, the appellate court held that § 11(B)(5) did not violate employer one's constitutional right to equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Orthopedic Hosp. of Okla. v. Dep't of Health


Case No. 100,354


COURT OF APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2005 OK CIV APP 43; 118 P.3d 216; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 28; 76 O.B.A.J. 1613



June 3, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] THIS OPINION HAS BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION BY ORDER OF THE COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS
Released for Publication: July 08, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE NOMA D. GURICH, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State challenged a decision from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff hospital in a fee dispute on the ground that Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 1-702b (Supp. 1999) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Under Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 1-702b (Supp. 1999) required new facilities to pay a fee to the uncompensated care fund. This was then distributed pro rata to other facilities in order to pay for uncompensated care. The hospital contended that § 1-702b was unconstitutional, and the trial court agreed. In affirming, the court determined that § 1-702b violated Okla. Const. art. 10, § 14 because it assessed a tax and distributed it to private entities without any governmental control. The fee in question fell within the definition of a tax, and there was no public purpose since private corporations were benefitted without any control by the State. Next, Okla. Const. art. 10, § 15 was violated because the distribution of the fee to the private corporations constituted a gift. There was no contractual obligation to provide indigent care. The court also noted that Okla. Const. art. 5, § 59 was violated because it was a special law imposing significant tax burdens on new facilities based on an arbitrary and irrational classification. Finally, the court was unable to sever the unconstitutional portions of the law.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Smith v. State ex rel. Dep't of Pub. Safety


No. 101,651


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2005 OK CIV APP 69; 120 P.3d 897; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 60



June 1, 2005, Decided  
September 29, 2005, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication: September 29, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE ROMA McELWEE, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellee driver was arrested for driving under the influence, appellant department of public safety revoked her driving privileges. The revocation was affirmed after an administrative hearing. On appeal, the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, reversed the revocation on the grounds that the department presented insufficient evidence that reasonable suspicion existed for the traffic stop. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the department challenged the trial court's reversal of the revocation of the driver's driving privileges. The appellate court found that the officer had reasonable cause to follow the driver based on information from his fellow officers; the driver was stopped when she made a right turn without using her turn in violation of Edmond, Okla., Ordinance § 10.32.060. The appellate court found that this ordinance did not comport with Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 11-604(A) (2001). But the burden was on the driver to challenge the presumption of validity of the ordinance; she presented evidence that she complied with the state statute and asked that it be noticed by the trial court. Nonetheless, the appellate court held that because there was no controlling precedent that the city's ordinance was preempted, then it was presumptively valid at the time of the stop. As a result, the traffic stop was valid even though the ordinance was inconsistent with state law, and the trial court should not have reinstated the driver's driving privileges.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

391 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Cherokee Data Computer Parts & Serv. v. Okla. Dep't of Labor


Case No. 101,181


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2005 OK CIV APP 81; 122 P.3d 56; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 66



May 27, 2005, Decided  
October 20, 2005, Mandate Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication; October 20, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE BRYAN C. DIXON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee company filed an action challenging the constitutionality of Okla. Admin. Code § 380:30-3-6. The District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, granted summary judgment in favor of the company, and appellant Oklahoma Department of Labor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The case originated from a Department wage claim filed by the claimant against the company. The company asserted and the trial court held that Okla. Admin. Code § 380:30-3-6 was unconstitutional because it permitted either the Department or a claimant or both to meet the primary burden of proving a wage claim. The appellate court found no error. The Department was a "party" to the proceedings as defined by the Oklahoma Administrative Procedures Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 75, § 250 et seq. (2001). The appellate court observed nothing inherently wrong with permitting the Department and a wage claimant to share the burden of proving the correctness of a previously issued order of determination. Thus, the Department was entitled to participate as an advocate in the wage claim hearing, and the amended rule allowing such participation was valid. Okla. Admin. Code § 380:30-3-6 was constitutional, and the appropriate standard of proof under Okla. Admin. Code § 380:30-3-6 was a preponderance of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Tillery v. Tulsa Christian Care Ctr., Inc.


Case No. 99,585


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2005 OK CIV APP 54; 118 P.3d 772; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 41; 76 O.B.A.J. 1884



April 29, 2005 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication: August 11, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA HONORABLE JANE P. WISEMAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED FOR ASSESSMENT OF APPEAL-RELATED ATTORNEY FEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant nursing home sought review of a decision of the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, which granted an award, pursuant to a jury verdict, in favor of plaintiff, the personal representative of the deceased patient's estate. On appeal the nursing home challenged the trial court's decision to award attorney's fees to plaintiff pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 1-1918(F) (2001) of the Nursing Home Care Act (Act).


OVERVIEW: The jury returned a verdict of $5,000 in actual damages and $40,000 in punitive damages to plaintiff. The trial court awarded $77,056 in attorney's fees, reduced from the plaintiff's initial request of fees in the amount of $115,375. The court rejected the nursing home's contention that it was entitled to have the reasonableness of the attorney's fees submitted to a jury. The record was insufficient to establish the nursing home's contention that negligence per se under the Act was not presented to the jury. The jury returned a general verdict and plaintiff was thus entitled to fees under the Act. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in assessing a reasonable fee amount that represented the complexity of the case and the time expended by plaintiff's counsel. The attorney's fee bore a rational relationship to the total damage recovery of $ 45,000. The award of the attorney's fee did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Okla. Const., art. II, § 6, because the decision to award successful plaintiffs under the Act, and not award successful defendants, served a compelling state interest to encourage private enforcement of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of attorney's fees to plaintiff. The court remanded the matter to the trial court to assess appeal-related fees to plaintiff.
