Johnson v. State ex rel. Okla. Dep't of Pub. Safety


Case No. 100,732


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION FOUR


2005 OK CIV APP 20; 109 P.3d 366; 2005 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 6; 76 O.B.A.J. 819



February 15, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 11, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF ELLIS COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE JOE L. JACKSON, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the District Court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee driver applied to have his revoked driver's license modified. The District Court of Ellis County, Oklahoma, declared that Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 6-205.1(A)(3) (effective 2003) was unconstitutional, and it modified the driver's license. Appellant, the Oklahoma Department of Public Safety, sought review of the trial court's order.


OVERVIEW: The driver had his driver's license revoked for three years. The revocation was alcohol-related. At the end of the second year of revocation, § 6-205.1(A)(3) was amended. The driver completed his incarceration, paid all fines, and attended all the classes that were required of him for his driving under the influence of alcohol convictions. The driver sought to have the revoked license modified so that he could drive to and from his work. The driver argued that the statute's amendment was an unconstitutional usurpation of legislative power over the judicial branch. In the alternative, the driver argued that because his license was revoked under the former law, he was eligible for modification under that statute, and the amendment did not apply to him. The appellate court determined that the driver had no constitutionally protected right to a driver's license. It was a conditional privilege subject to suspension. Further, the legislature's revocation, with no room for modification, was a rational and reasonable remedy to promote the public policy of highway safety.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's order.

State ex rel. Okla. Bd. of Med. Licensure & Supervision v. Litchfield


Case No. 98,927,


COURT OF APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA

September 14, 2004.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician challenged a decision from appellee Oklahoma State Board of Medical Licensure and Supervision, which suspended his medical license.


OVERVIEW: The physician, an anesthesiologist, was a partner in a chiropractic clinic. He engaged in several acts relating to prescriptions. Thereafter, the Board filed a complaint against the physician alleging unprofessional conduct. After his license was suspended for one year, the physician sought review. On appeal, the court determined that the record supported the finding that the physician allowed a receptionist and a chiropractor to stamp his signatures on prescriptions, which constituted aiding and abetting the unlicensed practice of medicine under Okla. The court noted that the Board had the authority to enforce Oklahoma Board of Narcotics laws and regulations under Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 503 (2001). Also, the physician failed to maintain records in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 509(19). The physician's due process rights were not violated, and sufficient findings of fact were rendered. However, the physician did not confess to a crime within the meaning of § 509(8).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the finding that the physician was guilty of unprofessional conduct based on a confession to a crime. The rest of the Board's decision was affirmed.

Horvat v. State ex rel. Dep't of Corr.


Case No. 99,976


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION TWO


2004 OK CIV APP 59; 95 P.3d 190; 2004 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 39; 75 O.B.A.J. 2011



April 13, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication by order of the Supreme Court, June 21, 2004.
Ordered published by Horvat v. State ex rel. Dep't of Corr., 2004 OK 52, 94 P.3d 80, 2004 Okla. LEXIS 55 (Okla., 2004).


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE GREGORY K. FRIZZELL, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which granted summary judgment to appellees, the Department of Corrections (DOC) and the Merit Protection Commission (MPC), in the employee's action for a declaratory judgment that the MPC's rule violated Okla. Const. art. V, § 46.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a permanent classified correctional security manager, received a letter from the DOC informing him that he was to be involuntarily demoted and transferred. The employee sent a notice of appeal to the MPC by certified mail. The MPC received the notice and dismissed the appeal as untimely. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in granting summary judgment against the employee on his claim seeking a declaration that the MPC's rule, which was that appeals were deemed filed only upon receipt, was unconstitutional. The MPC's rule violated Okla. Const. art. V, § 46. The rule created an unnecessary burden on those employees who lived far away from the state capitol and placed them at a disadvantage to those who lived near the capitol. Moreover, the MPC put forth no argument that application of the mailbox rule would create any burden on its operations. The court ruled that the mailbox rule, under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 990A(B), applied to the MPC appeals. The mailbox rule specified that the date of filing or the date of mailing, as shown by the postmark affixed by the post office, constituted the date of filing of the petition in error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause with directions that the trial court enter a judgment for the employee and directing the MPC to allow his appeal to proceed.

 

396 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Celestica Inc. v. Hines


No. 99,354


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2004 OK CIV APP 22; 86 P.3d 1095; 2003 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 129; 75 O.B.A.J. 878



December 18, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Writ Certiorari Denied February 23, 2004. Released for Publication February 27, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING TO REVIEW AN ORDER OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT. HONORABLE JERRY L. SALYER, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, employer and employer's workers' compensation insurer, sought review of an order of the Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Court which found that respondent employee had sustained a work-related cumulative trauma injury and ordered the employer, as the employee's last employer for more than 90 days, to pay all of the compensation award.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a claim in February 2003 that she suffered cumulative trauma injuries to the hands, arms, and shoulders while employed at her prior job and her current job with the employer. The employee listed November 2001 as the date of last exposure, but indicated the injury was aggravated in April 2002. The employer denied that the employee had sustained an injury arising out of and in the course of her employment. The workers' compensation court held that the employee had sustained cumulative trauma to the identified body parts from 1996 through her employment with the employer. The workers' compensation court applied Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 11 (B)(5) (2001) and held the employer liable for all the benefits it awarded. There was no dispute that the employee had worked for the employer more than 90 days when she made her claim. The appellate court affirmed the judgment and held that application of the "last exposure doctrine" to cumulative trauma injuries was proper. Further, as the employee became aware of her injuries after the enactment of § 11(B)(5), there was no impermissible retroactive application of the statute to the employer.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the workers' compensation court was affirmed.

 

397 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Norman Homeowners Ass'n v. City of Norman


Case No. 98,672


COURT OF APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


2004 OK CIV APP 14; 85 P.3d 853; 2003 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 120; 75 O.B.A.J. 640



October 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 29, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CLEVELAND COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE TOM A. LUCAS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners association sought declaratory judgment from the District Court of Cleveland County, Oklahoma, barring defendant city from enforcing against construction of new residences a tax designed to finance improvements to, and expansion of, the city's wastewater system. The trial court granted the city's motion for summary judgment. The association appealed.


OVERVIEW: The association argued that, because the city levied the excise tax ordinance when it issued a building permit, the tax was properly classified as an ad valorem tax upon property and was thus invalid under Oklahoma law. The court disagreed and affirmed the summary judgment granted to the city. The court stated that the excise tax ordinance came into play based only on the single event of a property owner's application for a permit to build a residence that would be served by the city's wastewater system. Therefore, the ordinance imposed an excise tax upon a particular use of property, and adoption of the excise tax ordinance was a valid exercise of the city's taxing power under Okla. Const. art. 10, § 20, Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2701 (2001), and Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2705 (2001). Additionally, the ordinance violated neither the equal protection provisions of the federal or state constitutions nor the unanimity requirement of § 2701(A), because the city could create classes of taxpayers for the purpose of financing improvements to its wastewater collection system and treatment facility where there was a rational basis for the classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Fent v. State ex rel. Okla. Tax Comm'n


Case No. 99,480


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION THREE


2003 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 135



October 23, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by Fent v. State ex rel. Okla. Tax Comm'n, 2004 OK 59, 99 P.3d 241, 2004 Okla. LEXIS 74 (Okla., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE DAVID M. HARBOUR, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, granted judgment in favor of defendants, state treasurer and other officials, when it dismissed plaintiff taxpayer's action for declaratory and extraordinary relief, by which he challenged the Oklahoma earned income tax credit (EITC) statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2351.43, as contrary to various provisions of the State Constitution. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued that the Oklahoma EITC, patterned after the federal EITC, created a social welfare or income-transfer program, affecting an impermissible gift of public money from tax receipts to a special class of individual recipients without a valid underlying public purpose. The appellate court agreed with the state officials and found that the state EITC was patterned after the federal EITC, and, as part of the larger state taxation scheme, had to be regarded as a tax refund. Funds held to fulfill the state EITC obligation never become part of state revenue subject to appropriation. The Oklahoma Constitution permitted the legislative creation of different classes of taxation, including exemptions and refunds. The EITC addressed the valid public purpose of economic stimulation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Estate of Cabelka v. Comanche County Hosp.


Case No. 99,072, Companion Case to Case No. 99,073) 1


1 The cases were made companion cases by Supreme Court order of April 24, 2003.


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2004 OK CIV APP 27; 87 P.3d 1101; 2003 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 130; 75 O.B.A.J. 1212



October 17, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 12, 2003. Certiorari Denied March 9, 2004. Released for Publication March 17, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMANCHE COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE C. ALLEN McCALL, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a decedent's estate through its personal representative and the decedent's children individually, sought review from a judgment of the District Court of Comanche County, Oklahoma, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, a hospital and various of its employees, including a doctor and unnamed individuals, in appellants' wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had previously granted summary judgment to appellees, based on appellants' failure to have complied with the notice provisions of the Governmental Tort Claims Act (GTCA), Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 152 et seq. (Supp. 1996). On appeal, the appellate court found that issues of fact precluded summary judgment as to whether appellees, through the hospital, qualified for the privileges of the GTCA. The matter was remanded to the trial court, which again granted summary judgment to appellees. On appeal again, the court found that the trial court correctly found that the hospital was a public trust created for public benefit, that the hospital was a political subdivision within the definition of Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 152(8)(d) (Supp. 1996), and that appellants had not filed written notice of their claim as required by the provisions of the GTCA. The court also found that denial of appellants' motion for summary judgment, based on their constitutional contentions, was proper, and that the hospital had properly responded to appellants' discovery requests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

400 of 423 DOCUMENTS


Steele v. Guilfoyle


Case No. 97,997


COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA, DIVISION ONE


2003 OK CIV APP 70; 76 P.3d 99; 2003 Okla. Civ. App. LEXIS 55; 74 O.B.A.J. 2468



July 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified September 5, 2003. Released for Publication August 29, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE BRYAN C. DIXON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed suit alleging defendants, the department of corrections and prison officials, violated his right to practice his religion because he was housed in a cell with a non-Muslim. The department and the officials filed a motion to dismiss and/or for summary judgment. The District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, granted the motion for summary judgment and dismissed the case with prejudice. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, claiming adherence to the Islamic faith, asserted violations of the U.S. Const. amend. I, the Religious Land Use and Institutionalized Persons Act (RLUIPA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000CC-1 et seq, and the Oklahoma Religious Freedom Act (ORFA), Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 251 et seq. (2001). On review, the appellate court found that the inmate failed to demonstrate that the department's policy of randomly assigning cellmates substantially burdened his right to exercise his religion: the policy did not inhibit or constrain the inmate's religious conduct; it did not curtail his ability to express adherence to his faith; and it did not deny him a reasonable opportunity to engage in those activities that were fundamental to his religion. Further, the department's policy of randomly assigning cellmates was reasonably related to legitimate penological objectives. As the inmate failed to make a showing of "substantial burden" under either ORFA or RLUIPA, he was not entitled to a declaratory decree that his rights were being violated under those Acts. The appellate court concluded that the trial court properly granted summary judgment as there existed no genuine issue of material fact.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
